Rita covers China for TechCrunch, tracking the technological intersections between China and the rest of the world.
Before her previous writing stints with Tech in Asia and TechNode, Rita managed communications for SOSV’s accelerators in Asia. At one point, she worked for a documentary production company and a mindfulness retreat center in New England.

Since Russian troops invaded Ukraine in late February, Delfast\u2019s top priority has been to see its Ukrainian team of 30 safely evacuated from the most dangerous parts of the country.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n When not focusing on sales, marketing, R&D and customer support, Delfast\u2019s smaller team of seven employees based in Los Angeles has been pleading with U.S. politicians and the European Commission to supply Ukraine with anti-aircraft missiles and fighter jets that could help Ukraine gain back some control over its air space, and, hopefully, put a stop to this war.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Delfast\u2019s co-founders, Daniel Tonkopi and Serhiy Denysenko, say they have always believed in safeguarding the future. When they founded Delfast in 2014, originally as a delivery company, Tonkoply and Denysenko knew that providing couriers with green transportation options would be critical to the company\u2019s operations.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n \t \n\t\t \n\t\t\tThe most important thing for an entrepreneur, and in general for any leader, is to protect the team and be completely honest with them during a tough time.\t\t\t\t\t\t\tDaniel Tonkopi, co-founder of Delfast<\/cite>\n\t\t\t\t\t<\/blockquote>\n\t<\/div>\n\t<\/span><\/p>\n The founders soon realized that a bike with the power, range and battery life their couriers needed didn\u2019t exist, and so they set out to build one. In 2017, backed by a Kickstarter campaign that saw the company raise $165,000, the startup began manufacturing a bike to fit its needs \u2013 one that promptly <\/span>won the Guinness Book of World Records<\/span><\/a> for the greatest distance traveled on an electric motorbike on a single charge.<\/span><\/p>\n More recently, the Delfast Top 3.0 e-motorbike <\/span>won Forbes\u2019 fastest e-bike of the year<\/span><\/a> in 2022 after the company announced some serious <\/span>upgrades to the vehicle during CES<\/span><\/a>.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n We spoke with Delfast\u2019s co-founders to discuss what it\u2019s like running a startup during a war, how the startup is considering breaking into new business verticals, and the importance of always having a Plan B.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n The following interview, part of an ongoing series with founders who are building transportation companies, has been edited for length and clarity.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n Note: Serhiy Denysenko\u2019s answers were translated from Ukrainian by a member of Delfast\u2019s team for TechCrunch.\u00a0<\/span><\/i><\/p>\n TC: Serhiy, you’re on the ground in Kyiv. What’s your day-to-day like?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. It\u2019s important to keep in touch and know that everyone is fine, or as fine as is possible right now.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n Besides my work as a COO, I\u2019ve been helping with volunteering, getting supplies and medicine to people, and this is something that pretty much every Ukrainian is now doing. I had my family relocated to Hungary, so I feel more or less safe, and I\u2019m just trying to work as much as possible and do my best in every possible area, whether that\u2019s supporting the company or supporting Ukraine in general.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n How are you managing your team through this crisis? What\u2019s changed?<\/b><\/p>\n Denysenko: <\/b>We got used to working remotely during Coronavirus times, so we have our task tracker, where everyone can see his or her task. Every Monday, we have an online Zoom meeting. Previously we only had these meetings at the executive level, but now during the war, we are gathering all together, just to see each other\u2019s faces and ask how they\u2019re doing, how\u2019s everyone feeling. Just to talk with everybody.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n <\/div>","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":" “Every morning starts with a check-in on Slack with all the colleagues. the robo-berry"},"content":{"rendered":" If you’ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that’s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren’t super good at because they tend to be… crushy. But this robo-berry<\/a> designed by Swiss researchers could usher in a new era of gentle, automated robo-pickers.<\/p>\n The secret to picking a raspberry is to grip it just enough to get purchase and then pull it downwards off the little stem, apparently called the “receptacle,” which seems backwards. Seems simple \u2014 and it is, but only our hands are among the most sensitive and finely controlled constructions in the universe, the culmination of a hundred million years of evolution, outdone only by (I suspect) raccoons.<\/p>\n Robots simply don’t have the senses necessary to figure out the perfect technique for picking a berry. But what if it could communicate with the berry to better sense the forces involved and avoid either a a brutal crushing or humiliating failure-to-detach?<\/p> <\/div>\n That’s what Kai Junge, a PhD student at EPFL in Switzerland, aims to accomplish with this “sensorized raspberry,” a silicone and silicon replica berry that provides feedback to the picking machine, allowing it to learn to pick faster and better \u2014 and cleaner.<\/p>\n “It\u2019s an exciting dilemma for us as robotics engineers,” said professor Josie Hughes, who worked with Junge on the project. “The raspberry harvesting season is so short, and the fruit is so valuable, that wasting them simply isn’t an option. What’s more, the cost and logistical challenges of testing different options out in the field are prohibitive. That\u2019s why we decided to run our tests in the lab and develop a replica raspberry for training harvesting robots.”<\/p>\n Apparently the hard part comes just at the moment of detaching, when the force needed to grip the berry on the receptacle suddenly becomes overkill as the object goes from solid to hollow.<\/p>\n The replica berry has a fluidic sensor that tells the system how much compression is being experienced by the silicone drooplets, allowing the control model to learn how to adjust its grip as if the berry itself is telling it how much is too much.<\/p>\n You can see the berry in action below:<\/p>\n <\/iframe><\/span><\/p>\n<p>The team plans to present their work at RobotSoft in April. And once the raspberry question is decided, they may move on to other berries, tomatoes, grapes&#8230; even apricots. The future is looking fresh!<\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>If you&#8217;ve never picked a raspberry, well, first of all that&#8217;s too bad, because a fresh raspberry is a beautiful thing. But second, and more immediately relevant in this case, you would not know that there is a technique to it that, surprisingly, robots aren&#8217;t super good at because they tend to be&#8230; crushy. -companies?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=8191"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=8191"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292389,"date":"2022-03-31T11:55:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T18:55:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292389"},"modified":"2022-03-31T17:57:31","modified_gmt":"2022-04-01T00:57:31","slug":"all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/all-eyes-are-on-swvl-as-it-starts-trading-on-a-spac-combination\/","title":{"rendered":"All eyes are on Swvl as it starts trading on a SPAC combination"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Mass transit and shared mobility provider <a href=\"https:\/\/www.swvl.com\/\">Swvl<\/a> went public today in <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. It\u2019s also a test for the company going public despite a market that\u2019s been unfriendly toward combinations with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, of late.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The Egypt-born and Dubai-based company has listed its shares at $10 on the Nasdaq through a merger with U.S. women-led blank check company Queen\u2019s Gambit Growth Capital. The planned merger, which will see Swvl offer 20-30% of its total shares, was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">announced last July<\/a>.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Following closing, the combined company, now \u201cSwvl Holding Corp,\u201d will trade under GMBT and GMBTW today before switching to SWVL and SWVLW on April 1.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292389\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl is the first company launched from Africa and the second Middle Eastern company to list on the Nasdaq via a SPAC merger<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. Anghami, an Abu Dhabi-based music streaming platform, <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">did so in February<\/a> when it listed with Vistas Media Acquisition at a $220 million valuation.<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/\">Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Egyptian ride-sharing company Swvl plans to go public in a $1.5B SPAC merger&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/28\/egyptian-ride-sharing-company-swvl-plans-to-go-public-in-a-1-5b-spac-merger\/embed\/#?secret=CnJTROn2h9#?secret=Q5eMhyfACo\" data-secret=\"Q5eMhyfACo\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Swvl raised $121.5 million in private investment in public equities (PIPE) for this transaction<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. The European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (EBRD), Teklas Ventures, Chimera, Agility, and Luxor Capital Group are some of its other investors. The company is currently valued at $1.5 billion.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In February, one of its investors, Atalaya Capital, pulled out of the transaction. And in a filing, Queen\u2019s Gambit announced the termination of forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreements worth $100 million in SPAC shares and an extra $2 million via a private placement.<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThe forward <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">purchase<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> agreement <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was done<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> with a group, and it was <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> access to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> capital,\u201d Queen\u2019s Gambit Capital founder and CEO Victoria Grace told TechCrunch when asked if the termination affects the deal.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cIts termination doesn\u2019t affect the valuation of the company or anything around our fundamental deal, which is Queen\u2019s Gambit merging with SWVL, so the valuation [stays] the same,\u201d she said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Investors withdrawing their interests and dollars from SPACs is not peculiar to Swvl. It\u2019s a usual occurrence &#8212; for instance, when BuzzFeed went public last December, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\">94% of the $287.5 million raised by the SPAC <\/a><\/span><a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/buzzfeed-suffers-wave-of-spac-investor-withdrawals-before-going-public-11638472756\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">was withdrawn<\/span><\/a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> &#8212; particularly as the SPAC hype gives way in the face of an underperforming market and tighter regulation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Despite the seeming setback, there\u2019s good news for Swvl. <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to CFO Youssef Salem, the company has an <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">additional $600 million from proceeds and<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> committed equity facility with B. Riley Principal to access over the next few weeks if certain conditions are met, he said.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Swvl was founded by <a href=\"https:\/\/eg.linkedin.com\/in\/mostafa-kandil-57761032\">Mostafa Kandil<\/a>, Mahmoud Nouh and Ahmed Sabbah in 2017. The trio started the company as a bus-hailing service in Egypt and other ride-sharing services in emerging markets with fragmented public transportation.<\/p>\n<p>Its bus-hailing services enable users to make intra-state journeys by booking seats on buses running a fixed route. Swvl offerings have expanded beyond bus-hailing services, though. Now, the company offers inter-city rides, car ride-sharing, and corporate services in the 10 cities it operates in across Africa and the Middle East.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The partnership between Swvl and Queen\u2019s Gambit came from a mutual interest from both parties<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">While searching for a company to <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">acquire<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl fit the blank-check company\u2019s criteria: strong business fundamentals, mobility and logistics (one of its core verticals), and an ESG ethos around women and affordable transportation.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On the other hand<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, Swvl &#8212; off the back of raising over $170 million in venture capital, expanding to over 16 countries across Latin America, Asia and Africa; hiring executives from Facebook, Uber and Optimus; and acquiring Shotl, Viapool and door2door &#8212; was on a quest for global dominance in the mobility space. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A SPAC with Queen\u2019s Gambit was the most suitable option for it from a financial standpoint, and both parties feel strongly about the sustainability angle around transport &#8212; Swvl claims it has prevented approximately 289 million pounds of carbon emissions since its inception.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The company plans to expand into several countries over the next six months, including Colombia, Mexico, South Africa, and the U.S. <\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In the meantime, all eyes will be on the company\u2019s performance as it <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">officially<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> starts trading tomorrow in a cooling SPAC market and a generally unsettled public market.\u00a0<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201cThere\u2019s a softness in the market, but as long as the company operates and delivers results, <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">maybe<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> today, people don\u2019t pay attention to it, but they will in months ahead,\u201d Grace said about the worrying SPAC and public markets.<\/span><\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">\u201c<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">I think<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> the market will change <\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">just<\/span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> like it always does and people go back to fundamentals at how we look at company\u2019s performances. For Swvl, they have been beating every single number that was ever presented to us. And that\u2019s what makes me super excited about this. And that\u2019s the type of target you want to partner with.\u201d<\/span><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/\">Almost everything you need to know about SPACs<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Almost everything you need to know about SPACs&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/21\/almost-everything-you-need-to-know-about-spacs\/embed\/#?secret=dbGVg33T0n#?secret=s9kBhwdIHM\" data-secret=\"s9kBhwdIHM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Mass transit and shared mobility provider Swvl went public today in a landmark moment for Egyptian and Middle Eastern tech ecosystems. /tc_video?tags=21691"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576814951,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/corporate-services\/","name":"corporate services","slug":"corporate-services","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576814951"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576814951"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576814951"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":52630,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/dubai\/","name":"Dubai","slug":"dubai","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/52630"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=52630"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=52630"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292372,"date":"2022-03-31T12:05:44","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T19:05:44","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292372"},"modified":"2022-03-31T13:58:42","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T20:58:42","slug":"microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-process-mining-vendor-minit-to-grow-its-automation-offerings\/","title":{"rendered":"Microsoft acquires process mining vendor Minit to grow its automation offerings"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Minit<\/a>, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which of those processes are ripe for automation.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Minit currently enables businesses to transform the way they analyze, monitor and optimize their processes. Minit\u2019s solutions have helped businesses gain deep insights into how processes run, uncover root causes of operational challenges and help mitigate undesired process outcomes,&#8221; Justin Graham, Microsoft&#8217;s general manager of process insights, wrote in a <a href=\"https:\/\/blogs.microsoft.com\/blog\/2022\/03\/31\/microsoft-acquires-minit-to-strengthen-process-mining-capabilities\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Microsoft&#8217;s corporate blog. &#8220;[With Minit, our] customers will be able to better understand their process data, uncover what operations look like in reality, and drive process standardization and improvement across the entire organization to ensure compliance at every step.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft dipped its toes into process mining with the launch of new features in Power Automate in 2019 and the acquisition of Softomotive, an RPA software provider, a year later. But with Minit, the tech giant is doubling down on a software category that could be worth over $11 billion by 2030, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wfmz.com\/news\/pr_newswire\/pr_newswire_technology\/global-process-mining-software-market-size-value-estimated-to-reach-usd-11-096-7-million\/article_a95b3354-ec2f-5389-b761-e4dbbdadbb97.html#:~:text=According%20to%20research%20report%20published,forecast%20period%202022%20to%202030.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according<\/a> to a report from Polaris Market Research.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292372\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>It wasn&#8217;t immediately clear whether the whole of the Minit team will join Microsoft &#8212; or, indeed, whether the company will remain spread across its current locations. (Minit is now headquartered in Amsterdam, with satellite offices in London and New York.) But CEO James Dening said that customers shouldn&#8217;t expect a change in the level of support they&#8217;re currently receiving.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are looking forward to what it means to become part of an industry leader like Microsoft and what that brings us &#8212; how we can use that scale and excellence to continue to deliver great solutions to our customers,&#8221; Dening wrote in a blog <a href=\"https:\/\/www.minit.io\/blog\/microsoft-minit-acquisition\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">post<\/a> on Minit&#8217;s website. &#8220;It has been a privilege to lead the company for the last year, and I\u2019m excited to continue my journey with the team, as part of what I consider to be the world\u2019s leading software company.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Microsoft spokesperson Zara Huang told TechCrunch that the Minit team will move into the\u00a0<span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> Process Insights team and that there will be &#8220;no change&#8221; to the current work location of Minit team members. <span class=\"il\">Microsoft<\/span> is in early stages of determining how Minit will be integrated into its offerings, she said, and the companies will share more details when they&#8217;re available.<\/p>\n<p>Minit, which was founded in 2015 by Rasto Hlavac and had raised \u20ac10.3 million (~$11.40 million) prior to the acquisition, is one of an expanding number of startups developing process mining tools aimed at enterprise clientele. Process mining, also known as task discovery, involves spotting root cause workflow issues and bottlenecks by pulling data from systems including desktop, email apps and workflows. It&#8217;s a key part of robotic process automation (RPA), a technology that promises to automate monotonous, repetitive tasks traditionally performed by human workers while at the same time generating logs to identify potential cost savings.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>As Protocol&#8217;s Aisha Counts <a href=\"https:\/\/www.protocol.com\/bulletins\/microsoft-process-mining-minit\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notes<\/a>, process mining has traditionally been done by system integrators who map out processes by analyzing manual workflows. Process mining software is designed to digitize the approach in a way that reduces the expense, time and effort involved.<\/p>\n<p>Underlining the appetite for process mining technologies, Celonis, a data processing company, earlier this week acquired Minit competitor Process Analytics Factory, which coincidentally integrates with Microsoft&#8217;s Power BI analytics platform. Just in the past several years, RPA vendor Automation Anywhere acquired process discovery and mining startups FortressIQ, Process Gold\\ and StepShot; Blue Prism released a task mining solution called Capture; and rivals including ABBYY and Kryon have expanded their process mining offerings.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/\">Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Celonis pushes into Microsoft ecosystem with $100M Process Analytics Factory acquisition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/29\/celonis-pushes-into-microsoft-ecosystem-with-100m-process-analytics-factory-acquisition\/embed\/#?secret=wqSRCOP7wQ#?secret=2NKiKfcj0k\" data-secret=\"2NKiKfcj0k\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;You know the process space is hot when even Microsoft, with its vast resources, has to buy its way in. I\u2019m sure Microsoft is seeing the same trends that we saw, which drove the combination of FortressIQ and Automation Anywhere,&#8221; Pankaj Chowdhry, EVP of discovery at Automation Anywhere and formerly CEO of FortressIQ, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Customers are starved for process data to help them navigate their transformation journeys and any vendor that doesn&#8217;t have best-in-class process capabilities will find itself challenged to offer a compelling solution to their customers.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Microsoft&#8217;s Minit acquisition comes at a time when the broader business process automation industry, which remains <a href=\"https:\/\/news.crunchbase.com\/news\/robotic-automation-is-back\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">flush with cash<\/a>, heads toward general consolidation. SAP acquired German process automation company Signavio in January 2021, just before ServiceNow got into the RPA segment with the buyout of India-based Intellibot.io. IBM <a href=\"https:\/\/newsroom.ibm.com\/2021-04-15-IBM-to-Acquire-myInvenio-to-help-Organizations-Use-AI-powered-Automation-to-Better-Streamline-Business-Processes\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquired<\/a> process mining software company MyInvenio in April. And Salesforce\u2019s MuleSoft and Microsoft followed suit with the purchases of automation tech providers <a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/08\/02\/mulesoft-acquires-rpa-provider-servicetrace\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Servicetrace<\/a>\u00a0and\u00a0<a href=\"https:\/\/venturebeat.com\/2021\/10\/22\/microsoft-acquires-clear-software-to-strengthen-process-automation-offerings\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Clear Software<\/a>, respectively.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Process mining, discovery and task mining has seen a lot of transformation with many acquisitions in the last year. [It] now appears to be maturing as a market and becoming commoditized under major automation platforms,&#8221; Saikat Ray, Gartner senior research director, told TechCrunch via email. &#8220;Gartner sees an emergence of automation platform vendors offering process mining and task mining as embedded capabilities, along with RPA.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated at 4:15 p.m. ET, March 31, with quotes from Microsoft and Automation Anywhere.<\/em><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Signaling its ambitions in the process automation market, Microsoft has acquired Minit, a Bratislava, Slovakia-originated process mining technology vendor, for an undisclosed sum, the companies announced today. Microsoft says that the purchase will &#8220;further empower&#8221; it to &#8220;help &#8230; customers digitally transform&#8221; by creating a more complete picture of their processes &#8212; and identifying which automation","slug":"robotic-process-automation","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449560943"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449560943"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449560943"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576598619,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/rpa\/","name":"RPA","slug":"rpa","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576598619"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576598619"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576598619"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":6,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/technology\/","name":"technology","slug":"technology","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/6"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=6"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=6"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2292473,"date":"2022-03-31T14:10:50","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:50","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2292473"},"modified":"2022-03-31T14:10:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T21:10:57","slug":"better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/better-learning-through-complex-dough-manipulation\/","title":{"rendered":"Better learning through &#8216;complex dough-manipulation&#8217;"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/20\/robotics-roundup-12\/\">focused on pizza<\/a>. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly straightforward platform onto which ingredients are added.<\/p>\n<p>I say \u201cfairly\u201d here because there are still complications. There\u2019s really no such thing as easy when it comes to building robots that can execute variations on a task at a large scale. Here it\u2019s the dough that presents the problem. Turning a soft and malleable ball of dough into a pizza crust is one of those things humans have figured out how to do efficiently, but it still proves difficult for robot workers.<\/p>\n<p>A team of researchers at MIT, CMU and UC San Diego set out to create what they\u2019ve deemed \u201ccomplex dough-manipulation.\u201d The system is separated into a two-step process, in which the robot must first determine the task and then execute it using a tool like a rolling pin. The system, <a href=\"https:\/\/news.mit.edu\/2022\/robotic-deformable-object-0331\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">DiffSkill<\/a>, involves teaching robots complex tasks in simulations.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2292473\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>MIT notes:<\/p>\n<blockquote><p>A \u201cteacher\u201d algorithm solves each step the robot must take to complete the task. Then, it trains a \u201cstudent\u201d machine-learning model that learns abstract ideas about when and how to execute each skill it needs during the task, like using a rolling pin. With this knowledge, the system reasons about how to execute the skills to complete the entire task.<\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p>The researchers say the system outperformed those trained in the more traditional reinforcement learning model. \u201cOur framework provides a novel way for robots to acquire new skills. These skills can then be chained to solve more complex tasks which are beyond the capability of previous robot systems,\u201d says CSAIL grad student, Yunzhu Li.<\/p>\n<p>This is robotics, so the whole pizza thing is really an initial problem for a system designed to tackle a lot more tasks. The company points to the emerging field of eldercare robotics as a possible use going forward.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A disproportionate number of the early industrial food-making robots we\u2019ve seen have been focused on pizza. I\u2019ve long posited that this is for two key reasons. First: People like pizza. We eat a lot of it. Americans alone eat three billion pizzas a year. Second: It\u2019s relatively easy to make. The dough provides a fairly Cribs","url":"\/shows\/tc-cribs","attr":"","target":"","classes":[""],"description":"","object_id":1605180,"object":"custom","type":"custom","type_label":"Custom Link","children":[]}]},"entities":{"posts":[{"id":2260564,"date":"2022-03-31T05:59:09","date_gmt":"2022-03-31T12:59:09","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2260564"},"modified":"2022-03-31T05:59:09","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T12:59:09","slug":"novaxs-biotech-raises-1-5m-to-make-injection-therapy-needle-free","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/31\/novaxs-biotech-raises-1-5m-to-make-injection-therapy-needle-free\/","title":{"rendered":"NovaXS Biotech raises $1.5M to make injection therapy needle-free"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A startup spawned from a lab at the University of California, Berkeley has won investor support to work on its patented needle-free injector, which it hopes can make therapies that traditionally require daily self-administered medicines less painful.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.novaxs.co\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">NovaXS Biotech<\/a>, founded by 21-year-old Berkeley researcher <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/alinasu\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Alina Su<\/a> in 2020, recently closed a $1.5 million seed round led by Lei Ming, an angel investor known for co-founding Chinese search giant Baidu in 1999. Other investors included Chinese venture capital firms Taihill Venture and NewGen VC as well as American ones: Courtyard Ventures, a fund focused on UC Berkeley startups, MHub Impact Fund, an innovation hub based out of Chicago, medical device maker Baxter, and Edward Elmhurst Health, an integrated health system in Illinois.<\/p>\n<p>NovaXS&#8217;s injection gun, which patients can snuggly hold in their hand, can push biologics into the body&#8217;s subcutaneous and intramuscular level within 0.3 seconds using liquid pressure. The device also comes with a cloud-based platform that collects patient information for physicians, like injection time, frequency, dosage volume, and medication temperature.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2260564\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The startup has found two early use cases already &#8212; in vitro fertilization and drug delivery for Duchenne muscular dystrophy (DMD). Su is particularly passionate about the treatment of the latter. DMD, an inherited disease caused by defects in a gene that encodes the protein critical to muscle functions, can put patients in wheelchairs by the age of 12. There is an existing FDA-approved solution that uses an Adeno-associated virus (AAV) to deliver modified genetic material to cells impacted, but the treatment can potentially <a href=\"https:\/\/www.fda.gov\/media\/151969\/download\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">generate adverse side effects<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Recent advancement in gene-editing technology has <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2016\/01\/01\/science\/gene-therapy-muscular-dystrophy.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">given the once incurable disease new hope<\/a>, though much needs to be done to actually turn the lab work into commercially viable solutions. That&#8217;s what NovaXS aspires to do, with Su bringing her bioengineering professor Irina Conboy&#8217;s gene-editing CRISPR therapies to DMD patients using the startup&#8217;s needle-less injector.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Many large pharmaceutical companies lack the incentive to fund IVF or rare disease R&amp;D because these specific markets have limited patients. On the other hand, smaller companies are lacking the resources to tackle such daunting tasks,&#8221; said Su.<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">NovaXS is targeting gene therapy and IVF at the initial phase because Su believes they have &#8220;the biggest potential to acquire a large market share.&#8221; It&#8217;s also planning to work on other diseases that require in-home injections, such as diabetes and growth hormone disorders in children.<br \/>\n<\/span><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>With the seed capital infusion, NovaX plans to work on the safety and stability of its products, apply for FDA clearance, and put together its core management team.<\/p>\n<p>Originally from China, Su&#8217;s other goal is to bring DMD gene therapies to her home country. The startup will still be headquartered in the US but conducting clinical trials for the DMD treatment in China, where local governments are luring foreign and returning science and technology talents with attractive money and policy support.<\/p>\n<p>Unlike in contested arenas like semiconductors and artificial intelligence, where tech transfers between the US and China are increasingly restricted, Su reckoned that in medicines and healthcare, the two superpowers are incentivized to collaborate because of a larger pool of clinical data is the basic staple of medical advancements.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We don&#8217;t want our research to just get published in Nature. We want it to be helping people in real life,&#8221; Su said.<\/p>\n<p>The business prospects of cutting-edge and still evolving technology like gene editing therapies can be hard to predict, and the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/06\/28\/theranos-founder-elizabeth-holmes-to-stand-trial-in-2020\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Theranos saga<\/a> has only made venture capitalists more prudent about esoteric medicines. But Su saw a silver lining.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The problem of Theranos isn&#8217;t its business but its science. We are not short of great scientists, but we don&#8217;t have enough medical talent who also understands business. We hope to fill the gap.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A startup spawned from a lab at the University of California, Berkeley has won investor support to work on its patented needle-free injector, which it hopes can make therapies that traditionally require daily self-administered medicines less painful. NovaXS Biotech, founded by 21-year-old Berkeley researcher Alina Su in 2020, recently closed a $1.5 million seed round engineering","slug":"genetic-engineering","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576594414"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576594414"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576594414"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576594414"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576594414"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":1460,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/healthcare\/","name":"healthcare","slug":"healthcare","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/1460"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=1460"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=1460"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=1460"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=1460"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2290478,"date":"2022-03-30T09:00:38","date_gmt":"2022-03-30T16:00:38","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2290478"},"modified":"2022-03-31T03:08:36","modified_gmt":"2022-03-31T10:08:36","slug":"equity-and-token-management-startup-sprout-raises-3m","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/30\/equity-and-token-management-startup-sprout-raises-3m\/","title":{"rendered":"Token and equity management startup Sprout raises $3M"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">As cryptocurrency goes mainstream, attracting <a href=\"https:\/\/www.pewresearch.org\/fact-tank\/2021\/11\/11\/16-of-americans-say-they-have-ever-invested-in-traded-or-used-cryptocurrency\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">individual<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2021\/11\/01\/business\/banks-crypto-bitcoin.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">institutional investors<\/a>, digitally-savvy employers realize tokens are an increasingly attractive form of compensation, especially for their millennial staff.<\/p>\n<p>But paying employees in digital assets can create all sorts of administrative hurdles. Human resources managers manually record who has been paid what on a giant Excel sheet but can easily lose track of where the tokens are going, as transactions are largely decentralized. And because token holders are also supposed to be shareholders in an organization, changes of ownership can tip the control and power within the company.<\/p>\n<p>Started three years ago, Sprout is trying to make the ownership of digital assets more traceable and transparent for organizations. The Hong Kong-based startup was founded by Andy Lee and Tony Sun, who used to work together at Mapbox, as a cap table software provider. It was helping mid-size startups keep track of equity as they grew, but last summer, as the price of Bitcoin shot to a historic high, the company began getting requests from its clients to help manage employee tokens.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2290478\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Sprout created Folium in light of this customer demand to help companies trace digital coins and non-fungible tokens across various blockchain platforms. Folium begins by collecting individuals&#8217; blockchain addresses, reading ledger changes and labeling them according to ownership, like whether it belongs to an employee, investor or founder, and the type of transactions; that is, whether it&#8217;s a payroll or investment.<\/p>\n<p>Once all the wallets are tagged, Sprout will have a token cap table ready just as it has done for equity ownership. Tracking tokens gives more transparency to founders, investors and ultimately regulators, reckoned Lee.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We think there&#8217;s a tremendous opportunity to help traditional and crypto companies manage tokens,&#8221; said Lee, who previously worked on Uber&#8217;s business development across Asia, including China. &#8220;Crypto is next-generation compensation.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Sprout has hit a sweet spot managing both traditional equity and the flourishing space of digital tokens via its SaaS platform. With this two-thronged strategy in place, the startup managed to raise $3 million from a seed funding round that recently closed.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Investors from the round included Sequoia Capital India, U.S.-based venture funds Sovereign\u2019s Capital and Firsthand Ventures, as well as Hong Kong&#8217;s NDN2 and the special administrative region&#8217;s government-backed funds. Prominent angel investor Ruby Lu, who is known for her early bet on Kuaishou, TikTok&#8217;s nemesis in China, also participated.<\/p>\n<p>Sprout is first going after companies in Hong Kong and Singapore, which have emerged as major nexus for crypto companies. &#8220;There are, anecdotally, a lot of employees and people in the Asia Pacific who understand tokens more than equity,&#8221; Lee observed. &#8220;So it&#8217;s actually attractive for a company [in the region] to think about, especially if they&#8217;re moving into web3, having tokens.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>With its new proceeds, Sprout plans to add more product and engineering staff to its current team of 30 and expand in Singapore. The company declined to mention how many customers it&#8217;s servicing but said Hong Kong-based microinsurance firm YAS Digital and crypto gaming company Animoca Brands are among its early users.<\/p>\n<p><em>The article was updated to clarify that Sequoia didn&#8217;t lead the round.<\/em><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"aP9cOhfJlS\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/09\/09\/tokens-can-better-incentivize-startup-employees-than-equity\/\">Tokens can better incentivize startup employees than equity<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; But paying employees in digital assets can create all sorts of administrative hurdles. glasses maker Nreal nabs $200M funding in 12 months"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">China&#8217;s augmented reality startup Nreal is on a roll. The\u00a0company, which hopes to bring AR to the masses by making bright-color, lightweight smart glasses, has just received $60 million in a Series C extension round, bringing its total funding in the last 12 months to a handsome $200 million.<\/p>\n<p>The new investment is led by Alibaba, which has historically been a more hands-on but less active corporate investor than its <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/07\/tencent-investment-2020\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">archrival Tencent<\/a>. The Chinese e-commerce giant has a reputation for acquiring controlling stakes in startups that can potentially be a complementary piece to its giant retail ecosystem.<\/p>\n<p>Alibaba&#8217;s investment in Nreal, however, is purely financial. In theory, the two could have generated strategic synergies. One could easily imagine Alibaba hooking Nreal up with its gaming and video streaming units, or even having it develop smart glasses for its millions of food delivery riders &#8212; who recently began <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/20\/end-of-chinese-food-delivery-platforms-runaway-growth\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wearing voice-controlled helmets<\/a>. But with the onset of China&#8217;s antitrust crackdown, the country&#8217;s tech behemoths have no doubt become more cautious with any investment that can be perceived as encouraging unfair competition.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2289870\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Plus, Nreal, which was <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/08\/china-watches-and-learns-from-the-us-in-ar-vr-competition\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">founded by Magic Leap veteran Chi Xu<\/a>, <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">already has a club of notable partners. Some of its strategic investors are Chinese electric vehicle upstart Nio, short video app Kuaishou &#8212; TikTok&#8217;s nemesis in China and Baidu-backed video streaming platform iQIYI. Qualcomm is not an investor but supplies cutting-edge Snapdragon processors to the hardware maker and works closely with it to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.qualcomm.com\/news\/onq\/2020\/07\/28\/mixed-reality-developers-get-more-tools-and-resources-nreal-ups-its-game\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">build a developer ecosystem<\/a>. Nreal is also backed by renowned institutional investors, including Sequoia China, Jack Ma&#8217;s Yunfeng Capital, Xiaomi founder Lei Jun&#8217;s Shunwei Capital, as well as private equity giants Hillhouse, CPE and CICC Capital.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Despite being China-based, Nreal hasn&#8217;t targeted its home market but has instead first tested the consumer appetite in six overseas countries, including <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/04\/nreal-raises-40-million\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Japan<\/a> and the U.S. The smart glasses maker has relied on partnering with local carriers to tout its devices. In the U.S., for example, Verizon is helping to sell <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nreal.ai\/light\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Nreal&#8217;s mixed reality glasses Light<\/a>, which has a relatively affordable price tag of $600 and can be plugged into a 5G-compatible Android device.<\/p>\n<p>With the proceeds from its latest round, Nreal will finally make a foray into China this year. The funding will also be spent on R&amp;D and growing its ecosystem of content and apps, which will be critical to user adoption.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"H9suzEUBRt\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/08\/china-watches-and-learns-from-the-us-in-ar-vr-competition\/\">China watches and learns from the US in AR\/VR competition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;China watches and learns from the US in AR\/VR competition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/08\/china-watches-and-learns-from-the-us-in-ar-vr-competition\/embed\/#?secret=jbNAs7QfZG#?secret=H9suzEUBRt\" data-secret=\"H9suzEUBRt\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>China&#8217;s augmented reality startup Nreal is on a roll. microblogging giant Weibo faces delisting risks in US"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">U.S. regulators have hastened their pace to enforce a law that could delist Chinese companies of which accounting papers can&#8217;t be inspected. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/hfcaa\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">The addition of Weibo<\/a>, the Twitter equivalent of China, to a delisting watchlist by the Securities and Exchange Commission could mean other Chinese internet giants like Alibaba and Baidu are not far from facing the same pressure.<\/p>\n<p>In 2020, the Trump administration<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/24\/china-roundup-a-blow-to-us-listed-chinese-firms-and-tiktoks-new-global-face\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> passed a bill<\/a> designed to tighten accounting standards on foreign companies. The law, which demands visibility into the books of U.S.-listed foreign firms, especially China-based ones, has not sat well with some countries that are wary of turning over data that could compromise their national security.<\/p>\n<p>China was one of the few countries not fully cooperating with the SEC&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/pcaobus.org\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Public Company Accounting Oversight Board<\/a>, which was created to audit foreign firms trading stocks in the U.S. But the reluctance is fading, as China recently told some of its largest U.S.-listed tech darlings, including Alibaba, JD and Baidu, to prepare for more audit details, Reuters <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/business\/exclusive-chinese-regulators-ask-some-us-listed-firms-prepare-audit-disclosures-2022-03-23\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reported<\/a> this week.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2288878\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Those auditing documents, however, won&#8217;t include sensitive data, according to the report.<\/p>\n<p>Many U.S.-listed Chinese tech outfits have already pursued <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/11\/17\/china-roundup-alibaba-secondary-listing-tencent-new-businesses\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">secondary listings in Hong Kong<\/a> amid rising tensions between the two superpowers. But Beijing&#8217;s latest gesture signals the country&#8217;s willingness to make concessions to keep its companies investible in the U.S. markets, which are preferable to many growth-focused internet firms.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"gdnNQ6ptLx\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/15\/china-tech-firms-challenges-2022\/\">China&#8217;s tech firms in limbo amid COVID resurgence, US scrutiny<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; EV chassis maker PIX raises $11M to build its own smart vehicles"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The autonomous driving industry in China <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/10\/china-autonomous-driving-2021\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">has enjoyed a boom over the past two years<\/a>, with both institutional and corporate investors pouring money into a driverless future. Companies thriving in the downstream, those <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/14\/2021-robotaxi-china\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">offering robotaxi services<\/a>, operating robo buses, or dispatching <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/25\/meituan-jd-com-and-neolix-begin-autonomous-deliveries-in-beijing\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">delivery bots<\/a>, have been particularly popular with investors, raising hundreds of millions of dollars and reaching massive valuations.<\/p>\n<p>The prospects of becoming cash-rich and a household name have lured some of their upstream suppliers to start building end solutions as well. One of these ambitious self-driving hardware suppliers is PIX Moving, a Chinese company specializing in automotive skateboards &#8212; a type of chassis that houses the batteries, drive units and other key components, and can be adapted to various kinds of self-driving scenarios because of its modular architecture &#8212; similar to what <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/08\/18\/electric-vehicle-startup-canoo-to-go-public-via-spac\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Canoo<\/a> does.<\/p>\n<p>Founded by former architect <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/chuanyu\/details\/experience\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Chuan Yu<\/a> in 2014, PIX recently secured 72 million yuan ($11 million) from a Series pre-A round, lifting its capital raised to $20 million, it told TechCrunch.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2288325\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>The company was part of hardware accelerator HAX&#8217;s second batch when it started out by building drone solutions. Five years ago it drove into the automotive space and has since landed a handful of customers across China, Europe, North America and Australia. Some of the big names include Alibaba, which uses its skateboard chassis, as well as Baidu and a Tier-1 German auto parts maker, which can&#8217;t be named due to a confidentiality agreement, that buys its ready-to-use robo vehicles.<\/p>\n<p>PIX is no longer content with being a white-label supplier, so it recently started <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/thepixmoving\/status\/1504095190432116739\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">offering self-driving vehicles named after itself<\/a>. Part of its new funding will go toward mass production for its own branded robo buses and skateboard chassis platforms, while the rest will be spent on ramping up production for its customers, overseas expansion, and hiring. It expects its production capacity to reach 1,200-2,500 vehicles this year.<\/p>\n<p>PIX declined to disclose the name of its single investor in the latest funding round, saying only that it&#8217;s a major sanitation solution provider in China with over 10,000 pieces of equipment deployed nationwide. The investment is meant to create strategic synergies, so PIX and the investor will jointly develop service robots for &#8220;environmental operation scenarios,&#8221; which could mean anything from garbage pickup to street sweeping.<\/p>\n<p>Asked how it plans to compete in an increasingly crowded self-driving industry, Nancy Lee, PIX&#8217;s international business director, said the company <a href=\"https:\/\/www.3dprintingmedia.network\/pix-moving-waam-to-reshape-the-future-of-e-mobility\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">uses 3D printing<\/a> to make customized chassis at lower costs and with less time than traditional manufacturers.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The company currently derives 30-40% of its revenues overseas but expects the ratio to reach 50% over the next two years. China might have been<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/10\/china-autonomous-driving-2021\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> a proponent for autonomous driving technologies<\/a>, but &#8220;complicated&#8221; traffic conditions in Chinese cities also make mass deployment of driverless cars challenging, contended Lee.<\/p>\n<p>PIX is curiously based in China&#8217;s southwest heartland, Guizhou Province, which is known for being a major hub for data centers like that of Apple. It also keeps R&amp;D and business development teams in Beijing, Shanghai and Shenzhen. Outside China, it has two part-time employees working for sales and technical support in the U.S. and is in the process of setting up a subsidiary in Germany to conduct manufacturing and R&amp;D.<\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The autonomous driving industry in China has enjoyed a boom over the past two years, with both institutional and corporate investors pouring money into a driverless future. Companies thriving in the downstream, those offering robotaxi services, operating robo buses, or dispatching delivery bots, have been particularly popular with investors, raising hundreds of millions of dollars tus":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/22\/chinas-ar-company-rokid-closes-110m-series-c-to-expand-globally\/","title":{"rendered":"China&#8217;s AR company Rokid closes $160M Series C to expand globally"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Chinese startup Rokid has been through a few stages of transformation over its eight years of existence, and it&#8217;s recently raised some new funding to stay afloat. The Temasek-backed company started out as a smart speaker maker when the vertical was all the rage in China in mid-2015s, but it has in recent years put more focus on augmented reality.<\/p>\n<p>This week, Rokid said it has secured a $160 million Series C round, lifting its total capital raised to $378 million. Between its last financial injection of $100 million in 2018 and this recent round, we haven&#8217;t heard much from Rokid &#8212; at least from the consumer side.<\/p>\n<p>While new players like Qualcomm-backed <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/04\/nreal-raises-40-million\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Nreal<\/a> have emerged to attract early adopters with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/01\/08\/chinas-nreal-raises-15m-to-shrink-augmented-headsets-to-size-of-sunglasses\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stylish, lightweight glasses<\/a>, Rokid appears to have kept itself busy by exploring enterprise use cases, like enabling remote communication for field workers in the auto, oil and gas, and other traditional industries. Its <a href=\"https:\/\/www.rokid.ai\/products\/rokid-x-craft\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">X-Craft headset<\/a>, for instance, is resistant to explosions, water and dust and comes with 5G and GPS capabilities. <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">And like many hardware startups that rushed to offer contactless solutions when the COVID-19 pandemic broke out, Rokid<\/span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/16\/chinese-startup-rokid-pitches-covid-19-detection-glasses-in-u-s\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> touted smart glasses that could detect temperatures<\/a><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> of up to 200 people within two minutes.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287601\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>With a team of about 380 employees, Rokid said it will spend the new proceeds on research and development as well as global expansion, so developed markets could be expecting more of Rokid&#8217;s B2B offerings. Indeed, the firm just <a href=\"https:\/\/twitter.com\/RokidInc\/status\/1504880455602085898\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">hired<\/a> an energy industry veteran to head its sales in the APAC region.<\/p>\n<p>The company declined to name the investors from this round, only saying they are &#8220;related ecosystem players,&#8221; which could very well mean clients and supply chain partners. It declined to reveal its post-money valuation.<\/p>\n<p><em>The article has been updated to clarify that Rokid raised a total of $160 million from two tranches of Series C fundraising.\u00a0<\/em><\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"xQ33kRSU7D\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/16\/chinese-startup-rokid-pitches-covid-19-detection-glasses-in-u-s\/\">Chinese startup Rokid pitches COVID-19 detection glasses in US<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; techcrunch.com\/?p=2287260"},"modified":"2022-03-21T13:07:38","modified_gmt":"2022-03-21T20:07:38","slug":"chinas-ev-upstarts-are-building-their-own-investment-powerhouses","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/21\/chinas-ev-upstarts-are-building-their-own-investment-powerhouses\/","title":{"rendered":"China&#8217;s EV upstarts are building their own investment powerhouses"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The investment game going after automotive startups is getting more competitive in China with not only established venture capital firms joining the fray but also industry veterans. Two mobility-focused funds that recently closed new rounds have the backing of the country&#8217;s leading electric car-making upstarts.<\/p>\n<p>Rockets Capital, a brand new venture- and growth-stage investment vehicle, announced earlier this month the close of its <a href=\"https:\/\/www.businesswire.com\/news\/home\/20220317005423\/en\/Rockets-Capital-Achieved-First-Closing-of-Over-US200-Million-for-Its-Maiden-Fund\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$200 million maiden fund<\/a>, with EV maker Xpeng as the anchor investor. Other investors are big institutional names in China, including IDG Capital, Sequoia China, GGV Capital, 5Y Capital and eGarden. The fund looks for opportunities in the auto industry value chain, clean energy and other &#8220;frontier technology&#8221; areas.<\/p>\n<p>The other major close from this week is Nio Capital&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/www.prnewswire.com\/news-releases\/nio-capital-closes-eve-one-fund-ii-at-around-usd-400-million-301506206.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">oversubscribed $400 million sophomore USD fund<\/a>, the Eve ONE Fund II. Investors range from sovereign wealth funds, insurance companies, multilateral financial institutions, funds of funds, family offices, pension funds to foundations from across the world.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2287260\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Nio Capital was started by William Li, founder of Xpeng&#8217;s archrival Nio &#8212; hence the name of the fund &#8212; although the investment body is <a href=\"https:\/\/ir.nio.com\/static-files\/cb42cc7f-6069-45a2-bbe4-21d4808609b8\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">not directly related<\/a> to the carmaker itself. The firm manages an RMB fund along with its USD one, focusing on auto, technology and energy sectors.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>Rockets Capital makes its connection to its EV investor more public. While it operates as an independent investment firm, it will also leverage Xpeng&#8217;s &#8220;industry expertise and resources&#8221; and &#8220;incubate technological innovation.&#8221; Given the stated mission, it won&#8217;t be surprising if some of Rockets&#8217; future portfolio companies also do business or partner with Xpeng.<\/p>\n<p>Founded in 2016, Nio Capital has a head start in the investment space. Some of its more notable deals in China include two leading robotaxi companies &#8212; <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/05\/momenta-500-million\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bosch-backed Momenta<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/robotaxi-startup-pony-ai-now-valued-at-8-5b\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Toyota-backed Pony.ai,<\/a> <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/10\/innovusion-64-millions-series-b\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Temasek-backed lidar maker Innovusion<\/a> &#8212; which is also one of Nio&#8217;s suppliers, BP-backed battery swapping Aulton and auto chipmaker Black Sesame.<\/p>\n<p>Over the past several years Nio Capital has built a fortress around itself with up-and-coming players in China&#8217;s auto industry. Now it&#8217;s time to see how Rockets Capital and its patron Xpeng play catch-up and what alliance it can forge to reshape the market.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The investment game going after automotive startups is getting more competitive in China with not only established venture capital firms joining the fray but also industry veterans. Two mobility-focused funds that recently closed new rounds have the backing of the country&#8217;s leading electric car-making upstarts. Rockets Capital, a brand new venture- and growth-stage investment vehicle,
