invasion of Ukraine has forced millions to flee their homes, fearing for their lives. But the war is also leading to Russians moving from their home country. I spoke to a number of Russian entrepreneurs and venture capitalists who shared why they have left or are in the process of leaving their homeland. But as they try to start anew abroad, anti-Russia sentiment and economic sanctions are set to haunt them.<\/p>\n<h2>The triggers<\/h2>\n<p>As Russia continued to amass troops at the Ukrainian border in mid-February, Eugene Konash, who had staff in Russia working remotely for his London-based gaming studio <a href=\"http:\/\/www.dc1ab.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Dc1ab<\/a>, became increasingly worried. But like many others, he didn&#8217;t expect a full-scale invasion.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2283795\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>His hopes of tensions fading soon evaporated. When it became clear Russia was waging a full-on war on Ukraine, Western countries began slapping sanctions on Russia. Businesses felt the impact right away.<\/p>\n<p>One of Konash&#8217;s employees found their bank hit by sanctions, blocking international transfers to his account. As the ruble collapsed, long queues formed outside banks in Russia as citizens scrambled to convert their savings into dollars &#8212; only to find hefty fees and the government <a href=\"https:\/\/www.nytimes.com\/2022\/03\/09\/business\/russia-ruble-central-bank.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">restricting access to foreign currency<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>The tipping point for Konash came when investors told him in no uncertain terms that his startup would be uninvestable if it continued to have such a heavy presence in Russia. His Russia-based team agreed it was time to leave.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The guys that even a month ago said they wouldn&#8217;t leave Russia under any circumstances were talking about grabbing their things and literally driving to Kazakhstan to cross the land border because the tickets to get out were either sold out or were super expensive,&#8221; said Konash.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Like many tech firms with an international footprint, Konash&#8217;s gaming startup hires developers across Eastern Europe for the region&#8217;s affordable and quality programmers. Originally from Belarus, Konash knows well that the former Soviet bloc nations&#8217; emphasis on science and math education has helped a world-class engineering and scientific workforce to flourish.<\/p>\n<p>Financial sanctions aside, it became impractical to operate an information technology company from Russia as foreign tech services are either banned or begin to retreat.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/04\/google-microsoft-sales-pause-russia\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Google and Microsoft<\/a> have suspended all sales in the country, while Russia has attempted to block <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/04\/russia-blocks-facebook\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Facebook<\/a>, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/14\/instagram-is-now-blocked-in-russia\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Instagram<\/a>, and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/twitter-russia-access\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Twitter<\/a>, albeit with <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/twitter-russia-access\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">mixed results<\/a>. Some users could still access these American platforms following the bans, suggesting that Russia may be some way away from having a robust censorship machine like that of China. Facebook and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/twitter-russia-access\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Twitter<\/a> said they were working to restore services in Russia.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Who knows when development tools like Unity may be blocked?&#8221; said a Siberia-born gaming investor who left the country following the 2015 Crimea annexation and subsequent economic sanctions by the West. &#8220;No one wants to end up in a country with no access to the outside world.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">The investor declined to be named, fearing the Russian government&#8217;s crackdown on dissenters. <\/span><\/p>\n<h2>Half foot out<\/h2>\n<p>After the invasion of Crimea seven years ago, many Russian-built companies began to incorporate elsewhere in a bid to placate investors with qualms over the political risks and optics associated with backing Russian companies. Before, many of these firms were operating outside the country merely on paper, with their teams often entirely still based in Russia. But the full-scale invasion of Ukraine has turned a trickle into a flow.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;After 2015, companies were drifting out of Russia legally,&#8221; observed an investor at a venture capital firm that recently moved its Moscow team out of the country. Even before the Ukraine crisis, the firm would only back a Russia-based startup if it was incorporated outside the country and had an international focus.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Physically, these startups would still be based in Russia. They&#8217;d conduct R&amp;D there because the cost of living was low,&#8221; said the investor, who asked for anonymity because the topic is &#8220;highly sensitive&#8221; for the firm, which has been trying to distance itself from Russia.<\/p>\n<p>Life as a startup incorporated overseas but operating for all intents and purposes in Moscow itself sounded pretty breezy up until recently, said Nikita Blanc, who four years ago changed his last name from Akimov. His company <a href=\"https:\/\/heyeveryone.io\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Heyeveryone<\/a>, which is building a tool to automate investor relations management,\u00a0is in the process of incorporating in Delaware.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2286982\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2286982\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout size-full wp-image-2286982\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nikita.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nikita.jpg 1280w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nikita.jpg?resize=150,113 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nikita.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nikita.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nikita.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Nikita.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2286982\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Nikita Blanc&#8217;s team working in Moscow before leaving the country following Russia&#8217;s invasion of Ukraine.<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The startup never intended to serve the Russian market alone, but Blanc and his wife picked Moscow as a base for the obvious perks: their parents could help take care of their 3-year-old daughter; the country&#8217;s internet was speedy, cheap, and free at the time; and Moscow was teeming with tech meetups where Blanc found like-minded founders.<\/p>\n<h2>The escape<\/h2>\n<p>The Blancs&#8217; entrepreneurial life enjoying the best of both worlds ended abruptly with Russia&#8217;s attack on Ukraine. Three days into the invasion, Nikita&#8217;s wife Valentina was lying in bed, devastated from seeing her country fall apart. She decided it was time to leave.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;I couldn&#8217;t do anything at work. Part of my family is from Ukraine,&#8221; she said. &#8220;It would be hard to leave with a child, but I didn&#8217;t think the situation would change. So we each packed 23 kilos of luggage and bought a one-way ticket.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>The couple moved with their young daughter to Georgia, one of the top destinations for Russia&#8217;s current talent outflow. It is a popular choice of country, along with Turkey, Armenia, Kazakhstan and Thailand, which are relatively affordable and easy to enter for Russians.<\/p>\n<p>The venture fund that recently left Moscow has been extracting hundreds of Russian citizens, mostly its own staff and portfolio companies, out of the country in the past few weeks. Across the internet, Telegram groups with tens of thousands of Russians discussing exit plans and helping each other out have mushroomed.<\/p>\n<h2><strong>&#8216;We Russians are fucked&#8217;<\/strong><\/h2>\n<p>The would-be \u00e9migr\u00e9s have to make escape plans on the fly as sanctions against Russia intensify on a daily basis: Which countries are still taking Russian flights, and how will they move money around?<\/p>\n<p>Sanctions continue to impact Russians after they have fled abroad, even those who left long ago. <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Notable financial infrastructure providers like PayPal, Mastercard and Visa have <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/netflix-paypal-adobe-and-others-join-tech-companies-suspending-business-in-russia\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">already suspended operations in Russia<\/a>, which means expatriates using Russian banks are not able to use their cards overseas. Estonia recently <a href=\"https:\/\/estonianworld.com\/business\/estonia-suspends-e-residency-applications-from-russian-and-belarusian-citizens\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">suspended<\/a> e-residency applications from Russian and Belarusian citizens to &#8220;prevent sanctions evasion and possible illegal activities.&#8221; <\/span>European Union regulators have <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/business\/exclusive-ecb-tells-banks-watch-all-russian-clients-widening-sanctions-net-2022-03-15\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reportedly<\/a> told some banks to scrutinize transactions by all Russian clients, including EU residents.<\/p>\n<p>The breadth of this wave of sanctions is prompting some to let go of their Russian passports. The Siberia-born gaming investor is seeking Singaporean<span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> citizenship, fearing that their Russian nationality might cut them off from the U.S. dollar-based financial system.<\/span><\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Ukrainians are accepted as refugees around the world, but we Russians are fucked,&#8221; the investor lamented.<\/p>\n<p>Others are betting that cryptocurrency can help them circumvent sanctions, such as the Blancs, who put a large chunk of their assets into crypto five years ago. Konash, the gaming entrepreneur, expected Bitcoin and Ethereum to be the last resort for cross-border payments if his staff get stuck in Russia for any longer.<\/p>\n<p>While major exchanges like Binance and Coinbase have <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/coinbase-not-banning-russians-using-platform-ceo-says-2022-03-04\/#:~:text=March%204%20(Reuters)%20%2D%20Two,a%20way%20round%20Western%20sanctions.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stopped short at imposing blanket bans on all Russians<\/a>, they have abided by sanctions to block target individuals. Binance&#8217;s CEO <a href=\"https:\/\/www.binance.com\/en\/blog\/leadership\/ukraine-russia-sanctions-and-crypto-421499824684903532\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">maintained<\/a> that crypto is not a likely escape route because transactions are recorded on publicly available ledgers, and hence easy for governments to trace.<\/p>\n<p>But EU regulators continue to <a href=\"https:\/\/www.coindesk.com\/policy\/2022\/03\/09\/eu-says-russia-belarus-sanctions-extend-to-crypto\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">argue<\/a> that sanctions imposed on Russia and Belarus extend to all crypto assets, and U.S. lawmakers <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/world\/us\/us-lawmakers-push-treasury-ensure-russia-cannot-use-cryptocurrency-avoid-2022-03-02\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">have urged<\/a> the Treasury to ensure Russia cannot use crypto to evade sanctions.<\/p>\n<h2>&#8216;Calm is the new currency&#8217;<\/h2>\n<p>Those who leave Russia face the obvious difficulty of being away from family and friends staying behind, but even greater anguish comes from the difference in their perception of recent events.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Our parents and older relatives keep telling us to go back, saying, &#8216;Everything is OK here. Russia is great,'&#8221; Blanc said with an incredulous but sad note.<\/p>\n<p>These educated, freedom-seeking Russian tech workers won&#8217;t likely look back. The Russians I spoke to, who are either leaving the country or helping others escape, were surprisingly calm as they recounted the woes of their country, in part because they have been mentally prepared for the inevitable farewell.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Our investor SOSV taught us to be like cockroaches, be flexible and adapt to new environments as entrepreneurs. This philosophy is now helping us go through these uncertain times,\u201d said Valentina Blanc. \u201cCalm is the new currency.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>\u00c9migr\u00e9s like the Blancs might well be the last wave of Russia&#8217;s chronic brain drain, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.atlanticcouncil.org\/wp-content\/uploads\/2019\/09\/The-Putin-Exodus.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">stretching back decades<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;The thing that gets me is that if you look at all the fantastic engineering and scientific talent that was produced in the Soviet Union and Russia &#8212; most of it has been leaving the USSR world at every opportunity,&#8221; said Konash.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Who does that leave in the post-USSR world? For me, this last wave of the brain drain is the death knell of the education and cultural scientific tradition that is probably one the few positive things to come out of the Soviet Union.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" Getty Images"},"authors":[133574232],"caption":{"rendered":"<p>MOSCOW, RUSSIA &#8211; 2022\/03\/03: People line up to withdraw U.S. dollars at a Tinkoff ATM in a supermarket on Tverskaya street in Moscow. The banks app allows users to track ATMs where U.S. dollars are available. Often, the information provided on the app is outdated or misleading. Yet sometimes it is accurate. Whenever it is possible to withdraw U.S. dollars, a line forms quickly as people queue to empty their accounts.<br \/>\nThe invasion of Ukraine by the Russian military has sent the Russian ruble plummeting, leading uneasy people to line up at banks and ATMs to withdraw US dollar as they worry that their saving would devalue even more in the near future. union","slug":"european-union","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/46740"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=46740"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=46740"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=46740"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=46740"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576669106,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/georgia\/","name":"Georgia","slug":"georgia","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576669106"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576669106"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576669106"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576669106"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576669106"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2286576,"date":"2022-03-19T05:50:17","date_gmt":"2022-03-19T12:50:17","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2286576"},"modified":"2022-03-21T06:15:57","modified_gmt":"2022-03-21T13:15:57","slug":"whale-dynamics-autonomous-delivery-2-5-million","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/19\/whale-dynamics-autonomous-delivery-2-5-million\/","title":{"rendered":"China&#8217;s driverless delivery startup Whale Dynamic targets US market with $2.5M funding"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">A nascent Nuro challenger from China has its sight set on the delivery market in the U.S. and just raised some seed funding to advance its ambitions.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"http:\/\/www.whaledynamic.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Whale Dynamic<\/a>, a Shenzhen-based autonomous delivery startup founded by Baidu veteran David Chang, said it has closed a seed round of about $2.5 million.<\/p>\n<p>Qianchuang Capital, a Beijing-based investment firm managed by veterans from China&#8217;s leading financial institutions, led the round, with participation from Shangbang Huizhong, a Chinese fund backed by real estate developers.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2286576\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Founded in 2018, Whale Dynamic is developing Nuro-like driverless delivery vans that are meant to do away with the steering wheel and driver&#8217;s seat. And like Nuro, whose delivery bots <a href=\"https:\/\/en.byd.com\/news\/byd-partners-with-nuro-to-manufacture-all-electric-autonomous-delivery-vehicle\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">are made by BYD<\/a>, it contracts a Chinese manufacturer to produce its self-driving vehicles, the name of which cannot be revealed yet as the deal has not been finalized.<\/p>\n<p>Whale Dynamic&#8217;s slight edge over Nuro lies in costs, surmised Chang, who worked as a product manager in Baidu&#8217;s intelligent driving group. Nuro assembles parts in the U.S., while the complete production of Whale Dynamic&#8217;s vehicles, from manufacturing to assembling, happens in China, which gives it a price advantage over its American counterpart. Its vehicles are priced at around $20,000 each.<\/p>\n<p>The latest financial injection will enable Whale Dynamic to expand its current team of 30 employees and explore product use cases in China and the U.S. Led by director of engineering Qi Wei, who hailed from Huawei, the company aims to have its first prototype car testing in some Chinese cities in May.<\/p>\n<p>In China, Whale Dynamic faces competition from retail tech giants like Meituan and JD.com, which <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/25\/meituan-jd-com-and-neolix-begin-autonomous-deliveries-in-beijing\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">started testing<\/a> their own goods-only delivery vehicles last year. Chang believes that his company&#8217;s technology, which takes the slower and more costly route of conducting R&amp;D and testing on passenger cars rather than building the boxes-on-wheels directly, can better stand the test of time.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2286957\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2286957\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2286957\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/4911647682698_.pic_hd.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/4911647682698_.pic_hd.jpg 5472w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/4911647682698_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/4911647682698_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/4911647682698_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/4911647682698_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/4911647682698_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/4911647682698_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/4911647682698_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2286957\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Whale Dynamic&#8217;s testing fleet using passenger cars<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>Chang eventually wants to base his firm in the U.S. and target express delivery services and supermarkets there. &#8220;You can test things much more quickly at lower costs in China,&#8221; Chang explained regarding why he started out in China.<\/p>\n<p>As regulators from China and the U.S. increase scrutiny over tech companies for potential national security risks, businesses that straddle the two countries will have to heed greater regulations or pick sides. TuSimple, a California-based autonomous trucking company <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/24\/tusimple-overseas-roadblocks\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">backed by an affiliate of Chinese social media giant Sina<\/a>, is looking to sell its China unit,<a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/exclusive-tusimple-explores-sale-china-unit-after-pact-with-us-authorities-2022-03-16\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> Reuters reported<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>Most of TuSimple&#8217;s vehicles operate in the U.S., with a smaller fleet running in China. But U.S. regulators <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/03\/24\/tusimple-overseas-roadblocks\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">have voiced concerns<\/a> over the firm&#8217;s Chinese background and its China office&#8217;s access to data, which reportedly led to TuSimple&#8217;s decision to offload its China unit.<\/p>\n<p>Security compliance is a priority at Whale Dynamic, Chang said. When it enters the U.S. market, the startup will opt for U.S. cloud services like AWS and Google Cloud; its China team will take care of hardware development only. The company&#8217;s key suppliers are also American &#8212; Ouster for lidar (and Israel-based Innoviz, which has offices in the U.S.) and Nvidia and Intel for chips. Unlike Nuro, which operates its own fleets, Whale Dynamic plans to only offer ready-to-use vehicles and software as a service, leaving the operational part to its clients, which should limit the amount of sensitive data the startup can glean.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"AUZDthUneC\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/25\/meituan-jd-com-and-neolix-begin-autonomous-deliveries-in-beijing\/\">JD.com, Meituan and Neolix to test autonomous deliveries on Beijing public roads<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;JD.com, Meituan and Neolix to test autonomous deliveries on Beijing public roads&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/05\/25\/meituan-jd-com-and-neolix-begin-autonomous-deliveries-in-beijing\/embed\/#?secret=nMwHegouzM#?secret=AUZDthUneC\" data-secret=\"AUZDthUneC\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>A nascent Nuro challenger from China has its sight set on the delivery market in the U.S. and just raised some seed funding to advance its ambitions. Whale Dynamic, a Shenzhen-based autonomous delivery startup founded by Baidu veteran David Chang, said it has closed a seed round of about $2.5 million. cars","slug":"self-driving-cars","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/9559353"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=9559353"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=9559353"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=9559353"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=9559353"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":183625,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/shenzhen\/","name":"shenzhen","slug":"shenzhen","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/183625"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=183625"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=183625"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=183625"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=183625"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":22728,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/sina\/","name":"Sina","slug":"sina","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/22728"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=22728"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battle tech firms in limbo amid COVID resurgence, US scrutiny"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">2022 is not looking any easier to many Chinese tech companies. The slew of new cyberspace regulations introduced over the past year or so, from anti-competition rules to <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/07\/china-roundup-game-algorithm-crackdown\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">restrictions on the use of algorithms<\/a>, has prompted internet outfits of all sizes to reshape their business models and monetization strategies, dampening investor confidence.<\/p>\n<p>New challenges that emerged at the beginning of 2022 have already spooked investors. The Hang Seng China Enterprises Index, an index for Chinese stocks listed in Hong Kong, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2022-03-14\/china-s-tech-rout-deepens-amid-lockdown-geopolitical-worries#:~:text=The%20Hang%20Seng%20China%20Enterprises,since%20a%20year%2Dearlier%20peak.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">plunged 7.2% on Monday<\/a>, the biggest drop since November 2008. Shares of tech giants &#8212; including Meituan, Alibaba, Tencent and Pinduoduo &#8212; have cratered over the last week.<\/p>\n<p>One macro risk that is causing investor panic is the resurgence of COVID-19 cases in China. The country has been recording several thousand infections a day in the last few days, an insignificant number compared to the rest of the world, but the worst it has dealt with in two years.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2284508\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Shenzhen, a major manufacturing hub and home to tech giants like DJI, Tencent and Huawei, has entered a one-week citywide lockdown. Foxconn, a major iPhone assembler, has <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cnbc.com\/2022\/03\/14\/apple-supplier-foxconn-pauses-operations-in-shenzhen-amid-covid-outbreak.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">paused productions<\/a> in the southern city of 20 million people.<\/p>\n<p>New outbreaks in Changchun have disrupted China&#8217;s automotive supply chains. The city in northeastern province Jilin is home to state-owned FAW Group, which is a joint-venture partner for Volkswagen and Toyota in China. Both Volkswagen and Toyota <a href=\"https:\/\/www.wsj.com\/articles\/covid-19-outbreak-shuts-down-some-china-factories-including-apple-supplier-11647246503?mod=hp_lead_pos7\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">have halted production<\/a> at their car plants in the city.<\/p>\n<p>A new wave of coronavirus has also hit Shanghai, which houses Tesla&#8217;s gigafactory, but hasn&#8217;t shut down the city&#8217;s business activities yet.<\/p>\n<p>If lockdowns don&#8217;t seem too damning for internet firms because the industry is well prepared for work-from-home, then the return of U.S. regulatory scrutiny may explain why many Chinese tech stocks have slid to their one-year low recently.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Last week, the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission<a href=\"https:\/\/www.sec.gov\/hfcaa#:~:text=On%20December%2018%2C%202020%2C%20the,%3A%20(1)%20is%20located%20in\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> named five Chinese companies<\/a> that could be delisted from U.S. markets. The action was backed by<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/05\/24\/china-roundup-a-blow-to-us-listed-chinese-firms-and-tiktoks-new-global-face\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">\u00a0a Trump-era law<\/a> that requires foreign firms to turn over audit information to establish that they are not controlled by a foreign government.<\/p>\n<p>American depositary receipts (ADR) of Chinese companies are stuck between a rock and a hard place. Washington demands visibility into the books of U.S.-listed foreign firms, but China<a href=\"https:\/\/www.chinalawinsight.com\/2020\/06\/articles\/corporate-ma\/the-holding-foreign-companies-accountable-act-and-delisting-of-us-listed-chinese-companies\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> bars audit firms from transmitting documents overseas<\/a>. This has long been a sticking point for U.S. and Chinese financial regulators.<\/p>\n<p>Beijing last year also <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/09\/what-chinas-new-data-privacy-law-means-for-us-tech-firms\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">tightened restrictions<\/a> on what data companies can transfer outbound, prompting a <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/07\/20\/china-roundup-data-security-clampdown\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">regulatory crackdown on Didi<\/a> following the Chinese ride-hailing giant&#8217;s hasty initial public offering in the U.S.<\/p>\n<p>Heeding delisting risks and geopolitical tensions between China and the U.S., many Chinese tech firms, including the largest ones like Alibaba, JD.com and NetEase, have pursued secondary listings in Hong Kong. The SEC&#8217;s move last week to name the five Chinese ADRs has clearly revived investor concerns and will hasten the pace of more Chinese firms seeking alternative market listing.<\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>2022 is not looking any easier to many Chinese tech companies. The slew of new cyberspace regulations introduced over the past year or so, from anti-competition rules to restrictions on the use of algorithms, has prompted internet outfits of all sizes to reshape their business models and monetization strategies, dampening investor confidence. ,"href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":576607387,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/pinduoduo\/","name":"pinduoduo","slug":"pinduoduo","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/576607387"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=576607387"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=576607387"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=576607387"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=576607387"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2283857,"date":"2022-03-14T04:27:13","date_gmt":"2022-03-14T11:27:13","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2283857"},"modified":"2022-03-14T10:05:43","modified_gmt":"2022-03-14T17:05:43","slug":"covid-rapid-tests-available-on-e-commerce-in-china-for-the-first-time","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/14\/covid-rapid-tests-available-on-e-commerce-in-china-for-the-first-time\/","title":{"rendered":"COVID rapid tests available on e-commerce in China for the first time"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">China is allowing the public to take COVID-19 rapid antigen self-tests for the first time as infection numbers <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/business\/healthcare-pharmaceuticals\/china-daily-local-covid-cases-hit-two-year-high-over-1500-2022-03-12\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">hit a two-year high<\/a> in recent days. Online marketplaces including JD.com and Meituan are now taking pre-orders for home test kits from government-approved manufacturers, including Shenzhen-based gene giant BGI. The products will also be available through drugstores nationwide.<\/p>\n<p>For the past two years, China has upheld a &#8220;zero-COVID&#8221; containment policy that has kept its case numbers low, but the strategy is increasingly tested by the more contagious Omicron variant. China has relied exclusively on the polymerase chain reaction (PCR) test, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.fda.gov\/consumers\/consumer-updates\/covid-19-test-basics\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a type of molecular\/nucleic acid test<\/a>, to identify cases, unlike Western countries that have adopted rapid antigen tests as a commercially available alternative.<\/p>\n<p>PCR tests, while widely recognized as <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cdc.gov\/coronavirus\/2019-ncov\/lab\/naats.html#:~:text=The%20NAAT%20procedure%20works%20by,sensitive%20for%20diagnosing%20COVID%2D19.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">more accurate than antigen tests<\/a>, require healthcare professionals to collect samples which will then be sent to a lab to get the results. Antigen tests, in comparison, can be carried out at home and generate results in less than an hour.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2283857\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>China&#8217;s drug regulator approved five COVID-19 antigen self-test products on Saturday, just a day after the country&#8217;s National Health Commission <a href=\"http:\/\/www.nhc.gov.cn\/yzygj\/s7659\/202203\/d4d7fb72088447f7a4f9cd10966a67eb.shtml\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announced<\/a> antigen detection had been added as an option of public testing.<\/p>\n<p>The introduction of self-test kits is not to be taken as a signal that China is relaxing its zero-COVID strategy anytime soon. The health authority stated that rapid tests are aimed at aiding the early discovery of COVID infections while nucleic acid tests remain the benchmark standard for case confirmation.<\/p>\n<p>At best, home kits will help take some pressure off an overwhelmed PCR testing regime. Local authorities in China usually order mass PCR testing whenever a few locally transmitted cases hit a city. In dense neighborhoods, residents often have to queue up hours for their swabs. The results from their PCR tests will then be digitally synced to a national &#8220;health code&#8221; on their phones, without which they&#8217;d be turned away by apartment compounds, restaurants, office buildings or public transport.<\/p>\n<p>Exactly how China will regulate the use of these self-test kits remain to be seen; for example, how does the government ensure residents will voluntarily inform the local authority when they receive a positive result at home? At least from what the <a href=\"http:\/\/www.nhc.gov.cn\/yzygj\/s7659\/202203\/d4d7fb72088447f7a4f9cd10966a67eb\/files\/8db5dd22ccb84b6296bc4257ba7db9c0.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">preliminary government instructions<\/a> say, home testing will still be monitored by &#8220;relevant administrative departments.&#8221;<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"qCDuJRfloL\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/08\/outrunning-covid-19-twice\/\">Outrunning COVID-19 twice<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Outrunning COVID-19 twice&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/08\/outrunning-covid-19-twice\/embed\/#?secret=ViLWplkWxe#?secret=qCDuJRfloL\" data-secret=\"qCDuJRfloL\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>China is allowing the public to take COVID-19 rapid antigen self-tests for the first time as infection numbers hit a two-year high in recent days. Online marketplaces including JD.com and Meituan are now taking pre-orders for home test kits from government-approved manufacturers, including Shenzhen-based gene giant BGI. The products will also be available through drugstores ":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/48383711"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=48383711"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=48383711"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=48383711"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=48383711"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2273684,"date":"2022-03-11T06:29:18","date_gmt":"2022-03-11T14:29:18","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2273684"},"modified":"2022-03-11T08:40:32","modified_gmt":"2022-03-11T16:40:32","slug":"makers-fund-mew-troph-metaverse-virtual","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/11\/makers-fund-mew-troph-metaverse-virtual\/","title":{"rendered":"Makers Fund-backed virtual social app MEW woos comic fans in the US"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Raven Gao didn&#8217;t set up virtual social platform <a href=\"https:\/\/mew.fun\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">MEW<\/a> to ride the metaverse wave. He began working on MEW in mid-2019 with a Tencent veteran because he wanted to build a virtual safe haven for socially awkward introverts like himself.<\/p>\n<p>MEW&#8217;s interface can be perplexing for many people at first glance. The lingo and aesthetics of the app have a clear appeal to fans of the anime, comic and gaming (ACG) subculture, Gao remarked. Cute anime-style images and creamy colors embelish the app and command buttons use terms more familiar to ACG fans. Rather than &#8220;signup&#8221;, MEW calls it &#8220;create your traveling file.&#8221; Users interact through interest-based hubs dubbed &#8220;strongholds&#8221; managed by other users, a design similar to that of Discord. Even the app&#8217;s name MEW, which is short for &#8220;Members of the Excellent World,&#8221; exudes an air of camaraderie for fantasy lovers.<\/p>\n<p>The first iteration of MEW launched in mid-2020, and its reach today is still limited. Several tens of thousands of users are active daily, though they spend a long time &#8212; 100 minutes on average &#8212; dwelling in interest hubs oriented around the usual suspects like games, movies, anime, but also more universal topics like self-improvement and football.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2273684\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Silicon Valley&#8217;s Makers Fund took a leap of faith in Gao in early 2020 when most Chinese investors thought the founder was &#8220;out of his mind&#8221; trying to build a new social network at a time the industry was dominated by giants like Tencent. In 2021, when &#8220;metaverse&#8221; became all the rage in both the U.S. and China, Troph, the parent company of MEW, suddenly found itself being coveted by investors at home.<\/p>\n<p>Troph took on more funding from China&#8217;s 5Y Capital and Zoo Capital late last year, bringing its total capital raised to date to nearly $10 million. The company has not previously announced its funding amount.<\/p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2283330\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2283330\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2283330\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-11-at-10.10.21-PM.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"522\" srcset=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-11-at-10.10.21-PM.png 1980w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-11-at-10.10.21-PM.png?resize=150,77 150w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-11-at-10.10.21-PM.png?resize=300,153 300w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-11-at-10.10.21-PM.png?resize=768,392 768w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-11-at-10.10.21-PM.png?resize=680,347 680w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-11-at-10.10.21-PM.png?resize=1536,784 1536w, https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-content\/uploads\/2022\/03\/Screen-Shot-2022-03-11-at-10.10.21-PM.png?resize=50,26 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" \/><p id=\"caption-attachment-2283330\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:<\/strong> Screenshots of the MEW app<\/p><\/div><\/p>\n<p>The world today has no shortage of startups claiming to be building virtual worlds and metaverses. But some of these products are &#8220;simply an avartar-based social platform mimicking the real world&#8221; while others are just &#8220;games with some social property,&#8221; Gao argued.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>MEW, in contrast, wants people to live out their &#8220;alter ego&#8221; online with complete honesty and comfort.<\/p>\n<p>Gao believes he has the right partner to carry out this vision. His co-founder Qiang Li spent five years at Tencent\u2019s QQ, the most popular social network in China&#8217;s PC era, where he led a front-end team building the messenger&#8217;s iPad version. Even today, QQ, with its many gamified features, remains largely popular among Chinese youngsters.<\/p>\n<p>MEW hasn\u2019t started monetizing, but Gao hopes to derive new forms of monetization beyond the conventional types for social networks like advertising, subscriptions and donation, by involving its users and sharing potential income with them.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We want to explore a model in which the users who make contributions to our product can share the rewards,&#8221; said Gao.<\/p>\n<p>Blockchain naturally comes to mind as a potential incentive mechanism. But Gao said in the short run, the company won\u2019t issue any coin offering or adopt blockchain.<\/p>\n<p>Troph&#8217;s goal this year is to expand to the U.S., capturing a similar game- and anime-loving demographic as it has in China. The company has around 30 staff in China now and is actively hiring in the U.S.<\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Raven Gao didn&#8217;t set up virtual social platform MEW to ride the metaverse wave. He began working on MEW in mid-2019 with a Tencent veteran because he wanted to build a virtual safe haven for socially awkward introverts like himself. MEW&#8217;s interface can be perplexing for many people at first glance. The lingo and aesthetics ch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557042"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557042"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2280723,"date":"2022-03-07T01:37:45","date_gmt":"2022-03-07T09:37:45","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2280723"},"modified":"2022-03-07T09:49:01","modified_gmt":"2022-03-07T17:49:01","slug":"robotaxi-startup-pony-ai-now-valued-at-8-5b","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/07\/robotaxi-startup-pony-ai-now-valued-at-8-5b\/","title":{"rendered":"Robotaxi startup Pony.ai now valued at $8.5B"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">China- and U.S.-based Pony.ai said Monday its valuation has surged to $8.5 billion after the first close of its Series D funding round, a sign that investors continue to chase a space where the mass deployment of autonomous fleets is still years away.<\/p>\n<p>Founded in 2016 and backed by Toyota, Pony is among a group of robotaxi startups that have set up testing and operational presence in both China and the U.S.; others that have done so include WeRide, Deeproute and AutoX. Pony was last valued at <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/11\/06\/chinese-autonomous-vehicle-startup-pony-ai-hits-5-3-billion-valuation\/amp\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$5.3 billion in late 2020.<\/a><\/p>\n<p>The new price tag is remarkable given some of the hindrances the company faced in the past year. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/11\/19\/key-executives-resign-after-pony-ai-combines-trucking-and-passenger-car-rd-units\/amp\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Several key members of its autonomous trucking unit\u00a0resigned<\/a> to join new rivaling businesses after an unpopular management decision to coalesce Pony&#8217;s trucking and robotaxi teams. The firm&#8217;s trucking force in the U.S. has since been dissolved, though it is still growing its trucking business in China.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2280723\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>In another turn of events in December, California <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/14\/pony-ai-suspension-driverless-pilot-california\/amp\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">suspended<\/a> Pony&#8217;s driverless test permit following a collision.<\/p>\n<p>As China&#8217;s regulatory scrutiny heightened over its tech companies, Pony <a href=\"https:\/\/www.reuters.com\/technology\/exclusive-chinas-tech-crackdown-thwarts-ponyais-us-listing-plans-sources-2021-08-11\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reportedly<\/a> had to halt its plans to list in the U.S., shortly after bringing onboard a former JPMorgan Chase executive as its chief financial officer.<\/p>\n<p>Building robotaxis is notoriously cash-intensive, but Pony said it&#8217;s well-financed. Trucking is also widely viewed as a quicker path for autonomous vehicle startups to pull in revenues compared to robotaxis. Following the Series D-1 round, Pony said it now has close to $1 billion &#8220;balance sheet liquidity.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Pony did not disclose how much it raised from this infusion but said it will release more information as the entire round closes.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>With a global team of over 1,000 staff, Pony is testing autonomous vehicles in four major Chinese cities (Beijing, Shanghai, Guangzhou, Shenzhen) as well as Fremont and Irvine in California. Its robotaxis have also been allowed to start charging passengers in a pilot zone in suburban Beijing, along with Baidu&#8217;s autonomous driving fleet.<\/p>\n<p>In terms of use of the proceeds, the startup&#8217;s CEO and co-founder James Peng said in a statement: &#8220;Our technical development and balance sheet strength go hand-in-hand in allowing us to significantly expand our hiring in 2022, open up a number of new autonomous vehicle global testing and operation sites, progress our strategic partnerships and rapidly grow our fleet.&#8221;<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"zyzCCyaj5W\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/10\/china-autonomous-driving-2021\/\">What&#8217;s driving China&#8217;s autonomous vehicle frenzy?<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;What&#8217;s driving China&#8217;s autonomous vehicle frenzy?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/10\/china-autonomous-driving-2021\/embed\/#?secret=EBCgizgqDM#?secret=zyzCCyaj5W\" data-secret=\"zyzCCyaj5W\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"16XxWIwuuE\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/14\/2021-robotaxi-china\/\">China&#8217;s robotaxis charged ahead in 2021<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; ype":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=449557111"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=449557111"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=449557111"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":17396,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tc\/","name":"TC","slug":"tc","taxonomy":"category","parent":0,"rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"submenu_categories":[],"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories\/17396"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=17396"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=17396"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=17396"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":2401,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/transportation\/","name":"Transportation","slug":"transportation","taxonomy":"category","parent":0,"rapidData":{"pt":"","pct":""},"submenu_categories":[],"_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories\/2401"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/categories"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/category"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?categories=2401"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?categories=2401"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?categories=2401"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2278322,"date":"2022-03-01T12:50:15","date_gmt":"2022-03-01T20:50:15","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2278322"},"modified":"2022-03-01T14:20:56","modified_gmt":"2022-03-01T22:20:56","slug":"bytedance-vr-pico-qualcomm","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/03\/01\/bytedance-vr-pico-qualcomm\/","title":{"rendered":"ByteDance-owned VR startup Pico strengthens ties with Qualcomm"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Pico, the Chinese virtual reality startup <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/30\/tiktok-owner-bytedance-buys-a-top-virtual-reality-hardware-company\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">bought by TikTok parent ByteDance back in August<\/a>, has struck a major partnership with Qualcomm to push further into the extended reality (XR) space.<\/p>\n<p>Pico&#8217;s XR products will be powered by Qualcomm&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/www.qualcomm.com\/news\/releases\/2021\/11\/09\/snapdragon-spaces-xr-developer-platform-launches-create-headworn-ar\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Snapdragon Spaces<\/a>, the chipmaking giant&#8217;s developer program designed to make apps more ready for extended reality. Rather than immersing people in a digital world in a virtual reality headset, the Snapdragon Spaces platform wants developers to build experiences for AR glasses and make them accessible through existing smartphones, making AR the &#8220;second screen&#8221; for users.<\/p>\n<p>The partnership doesn&#8217;t come as a surprise given the relationship between Pico and Qualcomm has been tight. Pico&#8217;s latest virtual reality headset Neo 3 already uses the Snapdragon XR2 chipset.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2278322\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>&#8220;This is a great opportunity. Maybe over a decade, [XR] could be as big as the phones, especially as augmented reality glasses become an extension of every smartphone,&#8221; <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=tMnMUKwnwDc&amp;ab_channel=ARMRXR\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said<\/a> Qualcomm&#8217;s CEO Cristiano Amon at Mobile World Congress, the major annual mobile connectivity show, this week in Barcelona.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We are excited we will be working together on hardware, software and technology roadmaps to enable the ecosystem for people,&#8221; Rubo Liang, ByteDance&#8217;s CEO, <a href=\"https:\/\/www.youtube.com\/watch?v=tMnMUKwnwDc&amp;ab_channel=ARMRXR\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">remarked<\/a> remotely via video.<\/p>\n<p>Despite being a leading VR brand in China, Pico is nowhere close to the scale of Oculus&#8217;s user reach or creator ecosystem. Pico&#8217;s two major products claimed a total of just about 0.3% of the global VR headset usage in January, according to <a href=\"https:\/\/store.steampowered.com\/hwsurvey\/Steam-Hardware-Software-Survey-Welcome-to-Steam\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Steam&#8217;s survey.<\/a> Oculus Quest 2 and Rift S together accounted for 60% of the market.<\/p>\n<p>Industry observers are waiting to see whether having a deep-pocketed parent like ByteDance would help Pico win a bigger slice of the market. At least in China, Pico is getting <a href=\"https:\/\/vr.ofweek.com\/news\/2022-02\/ART-815014-8420-30551149.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a slew of ads<\/a> on Douyin, TikTok&#8217;s Chinese version.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>The Qualcomm partnership could give Pico&#8217;s content ecosystem a boost and attract developers eyeing China&#8217;s XR market, which is <a href=\"https:\/\/www.counterpointresearch.com\/xr-vrar-headset-shipments-grow-10-times-cross-100-million-units-2025\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">expected to see significant growth<\/a> given the country&#8217;s aggressive 5G rollout. According to Qualcomm, Snapdragon Spaces is the &#8220;first headworn AR platform optimized for AR Glasses tethered to smartphones with an OpenXR conformant runtime.&#8221; It also includes handy developer kits for mainstream 3D engines, including Unity and Epic Games\u2019 Unreal.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"maO4WRQnr1\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/08\/china-watches-and-learns-from-the-us-in-ar-vr-competition\/\">China watches and learns from the US in AR\/VR competition<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;China watches and learns from the US in AR\/VR competition&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/12\/08\/china-watches-and-learns-from-the-us-in-ar-vr-competition\/embed\/#?secret=7XC0yFhgnf#?secret=maO4WRQnr1\" data-secret=\"maO4WRQnr1\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Pico, the Chinese virtual reality startup bought by TikTok parent ByteDance back in August, has struck a major partnership with Qualcomm to push further into the extended reality (XR) space. Pico&#8217;s XR products will be powered by Qualcomm&#8217;s Snapdragon Spaces, the chipmaking giant&#8217;s developer program designed to make apps more ready for extended reality. social media giants remove &#8216;inappropriate&#8217; Ukraine content"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">China <a href=\"http:\/\/www.china-embassy.org\/eng\/lcbt\/wjbfyrbt\/202202\/t20220228_10646378.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">has stuck to its position<\/a> of refusing to call Russia&#8217;s military actions in Ukraine an &#8220;invasion&#8221; or condemn Moscow, but its people are taking to social media to express their feelings about the war.<\/p>\n<p>Over the past few days, Ukraine-related topics have become some of the top trending hashtags on Weibo, the bellwether for public discussion on the country&#8217;s internet. In the meantime, Chinese social media giants have started to clamp down on &#8220;inappropriate&#8221; and &#8220;misleading&#8221; information related to Ukraine in the days after Russia&#8217;s attack on the country.<\/p>\n<p>Weibo, China&#8217;s equivalent of Twitter, had removed more than 4,000 posts deemed to have &#8220;provoked war, made fun of the war, or spread vulgar content,&#8221; the company said in an <a href=\"https:\/\/m.weibo.cn\/status\/4741583183812388?wm=3333_2001&amp;from=10C1293010&amp;sourcetype=weixin\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announcement<\/a> over the weekend. Douyin, TikTok&#8217;s Chinese version, removed <a href=\"https:\/\/mp.weixin.qq.com\/s\/jIH2McnAs_de10aCZ5qr-A\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">over 3,500 videos<\/a> that included &#8220;vulgarity, content that trivialized the war, incendiary information, and unfriendly comments.&#8221;<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2277537\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Scores of posts surfaced on Weibo calling on &#8220;Ukraine&#8217;s beautiful women&#8221; to go to China. Some users fabricated false information claiming that enlisting to fight in Ukraine could help one &#8220;earn course credit,&#8221; according to a <a href=\"https:\/\/mp.weixin.qq.com\/s\/sUTm_vfmlM361MjsI25iWg\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">notice<\/a> from WeChat. On Douyin, hundreds of click-bait posts misleadingly told users that typing in &#8220;Ukraine&#8221; would generate &#8220;explosive effects&#8221; on the short-video app.<\/p>\n<p>Other users have resisted such trivializing content, calling for more empathy for the war in Ukraine.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;Peace doesn&#8217;t come easy. We need to respect and value life,&#8221; WeChat said in its statement. &#8220;We are calling on all online users to keep an objective and rational attitude toward hot-button global issues, be reasonable when participating in discussions, and together preserve a clean and bright cyber environment.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>China has stuck to its position of refusing to call Russia&#8217;s military actions in Ukraine an &#8220;invasion&#8221; or condemn Moscow, but its people are taking to social media to express their feelings about the war. Over the past few days, Ukraine-related topics have become some of the top trending hashtags on Weibo, the bellwether for -companies?tags=22735"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=22735"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=22735"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":32758280,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/wechat\/","name":"WeChat","slug":"wechat","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/32758280"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=32758280"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=32758280"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=32758280"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=32758280"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}},{"id":2962992,"link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/tag\/weibo\/","name":"Weibo","slug":"weibo","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/2962992"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=2962992"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=2962992"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=2962992"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=2962992"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2274691,"date":"2022-02-20T01:00:37","date_gmt":"2022-02-20T09:00:37","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2274691"},"modified":"2022-02-20T19:03:30","modified_gmt":"2022-02-21T03:03:30","slug":"end-of-chinese-food-delivery-platforms-runaway-growth","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/20\/end-of-chinese-food-delivery-platforms-runaway-growth\/","title":{"rendered":"New regulation in China to hit food delivery giants&#8217; profit model"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Between 2016 and 2020, the number of people who ordered food online in China <a href=\"http:\/\/www.cac.gov.cn\/pdf\/web\/viewer.html?file=http:\/\/www.cac.gov.cn\/rootimages\/uploadimg\/1613923424818332\/1613923424818332.pdf?filepath=ZBWvETi1XzcBKtOIkqelkJJ4Vn5uw9ZthCXJtWLSr0nQACMKH6Ejiw\/UpdBYAwmsV5if6BYGd60xaZUMhKPZmjEjTcORl73kmCTdYOvdSjs=&amp;fText=%E7%AC%AC47%E6%AC%A1%E4%B8%AD%E5%9B%BD%E4%BA%92%E8%81%94%E7%BD%91%E7%BB%9C%E5%8F%91%E5%B1%95%E7%8A%B6%E5%86%B5%E7%BB%9F%E8%AE%A1%E6%8A%A5%E5%91%8A-0203%EF%BC%88%E6%89%93%E5%8D%B0%E7%94%9F%E6%88%90%EF%BC%89\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">doubled<\/a> to 400 million. The boom was in part thanks to the generous subsidies shelled out by the country&#8217;s food delivery contenders for customers and businesses. As two companies, Meituan and Ele.me, came to dominate the market, they began to raise fees on merchants. But a new regulatory change is about to hobble their profit model.<\/p>\n<p>On Friday, a group of Chinese authorities <a href=\"https:\/\/www.ndrc.gov.cn\/xxgk\/zcfb\/tz\/202202\/P020220218522078793799.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">announced<\/a> that food delivery platforms should further reduce the service fees charged to restaurants in order to lower the operating costs for food and beverage businesses. The news sent Meituan&#8217;s stock down more than 15% on Friday, erasing over $25 billion in market value. Alibaba, which operates Meituan&#8217;s archrival Ele.me, saw its shares slide about 4%.<\/p>\n<p>The proposal came in a directive led by China\u2019s National Development and Reform Commission, the country&#8217;s state planner, to &#8220;help struggling service industries recover.&#8221; The new rule <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">will likely taper the profits of the internet behemoths in the long run. Commissions contributed <\/span><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"http:\/\/media-meituan.todayir.com\/202111301644161764621862_en.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">as much as 60%<\/a><span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> to Meituan&#8217;s revenues in the three months ended September 2021. The firm also charges commissions from other types of merchants like hotels, though food delivery remains its largest revenue driver. Food delivery has been one of Alibaba&#8217;s main businesses following the firm&#8217;s <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2018\/02\/27\/alibaba-ele-me-plate-up\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">acquisition of Ele.me in 2018<\/a>, but e-commerce is still the giant&#8217;s main revenue engine.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2274691\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>China&#8217;s food delivery platforms have grappled with other changes that could erode their profitability. A viral article from 2020<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/08\/viral-article-puts-brakes-on-chinas-food-delivery-frenzy\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> brought to light<\/a> the high-stress environment that put China&#8217;s millions of food delivery workers in danger. Efficiency-optimizing algorithms that don&#8217;t fully factor in human capacity and road incidents mean riders are often running the light to complete assignments.<\/p>\n<p>Chinese authorities have ordered food delivery platforms to improve the safety of their workers. Meituan and Alibaba began giving riders connected helmets that come with voice command functions, so drivers won&#8217;t need to check their phones while dashing down the street on their scooters. The platforms have also relaxed delivery time limits for riders. The challenge for Meituan and Ele.me is how to balance workers&#8217; well-being and business profitability.<\/p>\n<p>Meituan is already working to reduce its reliance on manual labor. It<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/12\/29\/meituan-food-drone-delivery-china\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> recently showcased<\/a> a fleet of food delivery drones that have been running small-scale trials in several Chinese cities. The flyer is in its early stage of product iteration and regulations for low-altitude drones are still taking shape in China. The economic viability of drone-enabled food delivery is also unproven. But automation is at least one way for labor-intensive, on-demand services providers like Meituan to test out a safer, more cost-saving future.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Om7y3GWwbd\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/08\/viral-article-puts-brakes-on-chinas-food-delivery-frenzy\/\">Viral article puts the brakes on China&#8217;s food delivery frenzy<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Viral article puts the brakes on China&#8217;s food delivery frenzy&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/09\/08\/viral-article-puts-brakes-on-chinas-food-delivery-frenzy\/embed\/#?secret=2aOtPVzRtk#?secret=Om7y3GWwbd\" data-secret=\"Om7y3GWwbd\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Between 2016 and 2020, the number of people who ordered food online in China doubled to 400 million. The boom was in part thanks to the generous subsidies shelled out by the country&#8217;s food delivery contenders for customers and businesses. As two companies, Meituan and Ele.me, came to dominate the market, they began to raise ordering","slug":"online-food-ordering","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/2184721"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=2184721"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=2184721"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=2184721"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=2184721"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2274299,"date":"2022-02-18T00:52:02","date_gmt":"2022-02-18T08:52:02","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2274299"},"modified":"2022-02-18T10:23:42","modified_gmt":"2022-02-18T18:23:42","slug":"volkswagen-in-talks-to-buy-huaweis-autonomous-driving-unit-report","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/18\/volkswagen-in-talks-to-buy-huaweis-autonomous-driving-unit-report\/","title":{"rendered":"Volkswagen in talks to buy Huawei&#8217;s autonomous driving unit: report"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The autonomous driving space might be seeing the marriage of two titans. Volkswagen is in talks with Huawei to acquire the latter&#8217;s nascent autonomous driving unit for billions of euros, Germany&#8217;s Manager Magazin <a href=\"https:\/\/www.manager-magazin.de\/unternehmen\/autoindustrie\/volkswagen-und-huawei-verhandeln-milliardendeal-in-china-a-2852b306-82ca-42e0-aa83-0e1be7f04039\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">reported<\/a> on Thursday.<\/p>\n<p>Huawei said it had no immediate comment when contacted by TechCrunch. VW China said it has no comment.<\/p>\n<p>The potential merger will be a powerful one. Huawei&#8217;s autonomous unit sits under the telecom equipment and smartphone behemoth&#8217;s &#8220;smart vehicle solution&#8221; business unit, which <a href=\"https:\/\/www.36kr.com\/p\/1723788083201\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">started only in 2019<\/a>. The founding of the smart car BU spurred much speculation over whether Huawei would develop its own cars, though the firm has repeatedly denied any manufacturing plans and said it instead <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/19\/huawei-auto-strategy\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">wants to be the &#8220;Bosch of China&#8221;<\/a>, or a components supplier for car brands.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2274299\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Huawei appears to have adhered to this strategy, at least so far. Last year, the Shenzhen-based company <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/19\/huawei-auto-strategy\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">showcased its automated driving solutions<\/a> that had been preinstalled in a mass-produced sedan from Arcfox, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/19\/huawei-auto-strategy\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a new electric car brand under Chinese automaker BAIC<\/a>. Huawei supplied the electric sedan&#8217;s chipset and in-car operating system.<\/p>\n<p>For VW, a tech firm with autonomous driving capabilities, this could help advance its ambitions to make the vehicles of tomorrow. Indeed, the German giant struck a partnership with Argo AI, a Pittsburg-based startup backed by Ford and VW. Last September, the duo unveiled the first product of their joint effort, <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/09\/05\/volkswagen-and-argo-ai-reveal-first-id-buzz-test-vehicle-for-autonomous-driving\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a self-driving electric van<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>It would surprise no one that VW was in search of a similar tech partner in China, its <a href=\"https:\/\/annualreport2020.volkswagenag.com\/divisions\/volkswagen-group-china.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">largest market as of 2020<\/a>. A number of China&#8217;s autonomous vehicle companies have already fostered deep relationships with automakers; Baidu <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/26\/baidus-electric-carmaker-jidu-series-a\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">has a joint venture with Geely<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/01\/10\/baidu-electric-car-making\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Didi has a JV with BYD<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>The reported acquisition comes at a delicate time for Huawei&#8217;s AV team. Su Jing, former head of the Chinese firm&#8217;s autonomous driving product, <a href=\"https:\/\/cnevpost.com\/2022\/01\/26\/huawei-confirms-its-former-smart-driving-team-leader-su-jing-has-left\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">left the company in January<\/a> after making what Huawei called &#8220;inappropriate comments&#8221; about Tesla, accusing Autopilot&#8217;s lethal accidents of &#8220;killing people.&#8221;<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p>Since his departure, the Huawei veteran&#8217;s next step has drawn much speculation. What we know is Su&#8217;s dislike of robotaxis. In<a href=\"https:\/\/finance.sina.com.cn\/tech\/2021-04-17\/doc-ikmyaawc0275912.shtml\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> an interview last year<\/a>, the outspoken executive said, &#8220;any company that sees robotaxis as its ultimate commercial goal is doomed. Those who will be able to deliver robotaxis will be the ones working on passenger cars. That market is definitely going to be mine, just not yet.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>An acquisition of Huawei&#8217;s autonomous driving business won&#8217;t be cheap. The company&#8217;s smart car unit had plans to spend <a href=\"https:\/\/www.cnbeta.com\/articles\/tech\/1116453.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">a total of $1 billion<\/a> on R&amp;D for the year 2021. It also aimed to build an R&amp;D team boasting 5,000 staff, with over 2,000 of them working on autonomous driving alone. The question is: Huawei has invested so heavily in smart driving already, with a growing pool of customers, why would it give this budding business away?<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"c7lSEqYweP\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/19\/huawei-auto-strategy\/\">Huawei says it&#8217;s not a carmaker &#8212; it wants to be the Bosch of China<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Huawei says it&#8217;s not a carmaker &#8212; it wants to be the Bosch of China&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/04\/19\/huawei-auto-strategy\/embed\/#?secret=Xiv36iFCWQ#?secret=c7lSEqYweP\" data-secret=\"c7lSEqYweP\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>The autonomous driving space might be seeing the marriage of two titans.
