Kong&#8217;s offline and virtual events platform EventX closes $18M Series B"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">As countries ease up on COVID restrictions, activities are going back in person. But the virtual event space continues to attract investors, at least in Asia. Hong Kong-based events management platform EventX said today it has raised another $8 million for its Series B, lifting the total amount secured for this round to $18 million.<\/p>\n<p>The new injection was led by GL Ventures, the early-stage investment arm of Hillhouse Capital. Previous investors include Gaocheng Capital, an investment firm founded by a former Hillhouse partner, and HTC, the Taiwanese electronics giant that has pushed into virtual reality in recent years. EventX declined to disclose its post-money valuation.<\/p>\n<p>The Series B came eight years after EventX was founded, an unusually patient fundraising pace compared to many cash-burning internet firms across the border in mainland China. The company started out by managing real-life events, from <a href=\"https:\/\/cn.technode.com\/post\/2014-03-04\/eventxtra\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">supporting user registration to helping attendees exchange virtual business cards<\/a>. When COVID-19 hit in 2020, it saw an opportunity to go digital, so it developed a new service akin to Hopin, supporting live events like webinars and virtual exhibitions. Today, the platform also has a lead-generation function, helping organizers develop new clients and partners through events.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2273037\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Thanks to pandemic control on in-person events, Hopin became <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/12\/hopin-into-lessons-from-peloton\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">one of the fastest-growing companies<\/a>\u00a0in recent memory. But news came last week that the London-based startup had <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/10\/virtual-events-platform-hopin-cuts-12-of-staff-citing-goal-of-sustainable-growth\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">laid off 12% of its staff<\/a> as it realized post-COVID demand for virtual events would slow. The pandemic was also a boon to EventX; its online attendees in the fourth quarter of 2021 grew by 120%. And even if live events resume their normalcy, the company believes it can cling onto its long-running offline business.<\/p>\n<p>So far, the company has helped organize events in more than 100 cities, mostly across Asia, and its platform has served more than five million attendees. Its team of 100 is spread across Hong Kong, Singapore, Japan, South Korea and Taiwan.<\/p>\n<p>The startup plans to spend its new proceeds on potential acquisitions, product development, recruitment and expansion in Asia, particularly Taiwan and Southeast Asia. It also has ambitions to bring VR solutions into its event experience by teaming up with its investor HTC.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Q14hghcZri\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/12\/hopin-into-lessons-from-peloton\/\">Hopin\u2019 into lessons from Peloton<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;Hopin\u2019 into lessons from Peloton&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/12\/hopin-into-lessons-from-peloton\/embed\/#?secret=NbBSRqu8No#?secret=Q14hghcZri\" data-secret=\"Q14hghcZri\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>As countries ease up on COVID restrictions, activities are going back in person. But the virtual event space continues to attract investors, at least in Asia. Hong Kong-based events management platform EventX said today it has raised another $8 million for its Series B, lifting the total amount secured for this round to $18 million. Asia","slug":"southeast-asia","taxonomy":"post_tag","_links":{"self":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags\/449557032"}],"collection":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tags"}],"about":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/taxonomies\/post_tag"}],"wp:post_type":[{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/posts?tags=449557032"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/battlefield-companies?tags=449557032"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc-media-gallery?tags=449557032"},{"href":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/wp-json\/wp\/v2\/tc_video?tags=449557032"}],"curies":[{"name":"wp","href":"https:\/\/api.w.org\/{rel}","templated":true}]}}],[],[],[],[]]}},{"id":2272378,"date":"2022-02-15T07:10:36","date_gmt":"2022-02-15T15:10:36","guid":{"rendered":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/?p=2272378"},"modified":"2022-02-15T08:52:46","modified_gmt":"2022-02-15T16:52:46","slug":"chinas-travel-booking-giant-trip-com-adopts-the-hybrid-office","status":"publish","type":"post","link":"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/15\/chinas-travel-booking-giant-trip-com-adopts-the-hybrid-office\/","title":{"rendered":"China&#8217;s travel booking giant Trip.com adopts the hybrid office"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Scores of tech companies around the world have switched to remote work or some sort of hybrid model during the past two COVID-hit years. In China, though, most tech firms have gone back to the office since summer 2020, thanks to the country&#8217;s low infection rates as a result of its zero-COVID policy. Despite the <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2020\/04\/08\/outrunning-covid-19-twice\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">normalcy of life<\/a>, one Chinese company decided to stick with remote work.<\/p>\n<p>Starting March 1, China&#8217;s largest flight and hotel booking platform Trip.com will let employees work up to two days a week from home upon permission, it announced Tuesday. The company, founded in 1999 and rebranded from Ctrip to Trip.com in 2019, made the move after seeing &#8220;improved wellness&#8221; in 75% of its 1,600 staff who worked remotely during a six-month trial last year. The experiment included staff with core technical, product, business and marketing roles and about 400 supervisors, a spokesperson for the firm told TechCrunch.<\/p>\n<p>As many as 93% of the participants <span style=\"font-size: 1rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">felt they used their time &#8220;more efficiently,&#8221; and the firm&#8217;s turnover rate, which tracks voluntary resignations, dropped by roughly one-third in the period. Nearly 60% said they &#8220;strongly&#8221; supported hybrid work when the trial ended.<\/span><\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2272378\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Employees can apply to work from home, a cafe or anywhere else of their choice from March on. Managers in each department will decide who can request to work remotely based on team targets and each person&#8217;s situation, said the spokesperson. The managers also have the right to make adjustments to the arrangement at their discretion.<\/p>\n<p>The hybrid practice will first roll out at Trip.com&#8217;s China offices, while its overseas branches will adopt the model &#8220;according to local circumstances and COVID-19 protection measures.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Trip.com, which is listed on Nasdaq and the Hong Kong Stock Exchange, has made international expansion by buying up foreign rivals over the years. In a<a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2016\/11\/23\/ctrip-skyscanner\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> $1.74 billion deal in 2016<\/a>, it scooped up Scotland-based Skyscanner. <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2019\/04\/26\/ctrip-makemytrip-naspers-share-swap\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">In 2019<\/a>, it increased its shares in India&#8217;s MakeMyTrip to nearly half. More recently<a href=\"https:\/\/www.travix.com\/press\/travix-part-of-trip-com-group\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> in 2020<\/a>, it bought Dutch travel group Travix for an undisclosed amount.<\/p>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/investors.trip.com\/static-files\/08bd6175-f635-419c-9b88-f9f4eefe79ff\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">As of December 2020<\/a>, Trip.com, its subsidiaries and affiliates had a combined headcount of around 33,400. Around 30,000 are in China.<\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<p><a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/james-liang-tripgroup\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">James Liang<\/a>, co-founder and chairman of the board at Trip.com, is a frequent commentator on China&#8217;s social issues. When conceiving the flexible work schedule, Liang, a computer scientist and economist, apparently had China&#8217;s demographic challenges in mind as well.<\/p>\n<p>In a statement, Liang said a hybrid workplace is &#8220;a multi-win for companies, employees and society. Not only does it improve employee satisfaction without compromising efficiency, it also helps reduce traffic congestion and environmental protection; alleviates high housing prices and regional disparities; and contributes to families, female career development and higher fertility rates.&#8221;<\/p>\n<p>Trip.com is adopting the hybrid office at a time the overwork culture in China&#8217;s tech sector increasingly <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/10\/bilibili-employee-death-996\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">draws concerns and criticism<\/a>. The firm shows that remote work doesn&#8217;t compromise productivity; 71.9% of the participants from its 2021 experiment reported hybrid work had no impact on their performance.<\/p>\n<p>&#8220;We hope that hybrid work models will be promoted more across mainstream Chinese companies in the future, which will have a positive and far-reaching impact on society and economy,&#8221; Liang said.<\/p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Rfe0utN5FI\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2021\/08\/13\/more-companies-should-shift-to-a-work-from-home-model\/\">More companies should shift to a work-from-home model<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; social network BUD raises $15M in Series A+ round"},"content":{"rendered":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Investors are justling to find the next killer app for the metaverse. <a href=\"https:\/\/www.joinbudapp.com\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">BUD<\/a>, an app that allows users to create their customizable 3D experiences and interact with others, <a href=\"https:\/\/mp.weixin.qq.com\/s\/xDdnHxSOozIPTTdsL9HE-Q\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">said<\/a> today it has landed $15 million funding in a Series A+ round.<\/p>\n<p>Featuring cuddly characters that are reminiscent of Animal Crossing, BUD only rolled out in November. Within weeks it shot to the top 10 social apps on Android in several countries including the U.S., <a href=\"https:\/\/www.appannie.com\/apps\/google-play\/app\/20600015777058\/rank-history?app_slug=20600015777058&amp;market_slug=google-play&amp;vtype=day&amp;countries=US&amp;view=rank&amp;date=2021-11-17~2022-02-14&amp;legends=222\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">according to<\/a> analytics firm App Annie, though its ranking has sunk to the 100s since. Worldwide, the app has maintained a three-digit month-on-month growth since its launch, the company said.<\/p>\n<p>The slowing momentum in the U.S. didn&#8217;t stop some of China&#8217;s most active investors from betting on the nascent app. Qiming Ventures Partners led the round, with Source Code Capital, GGV Capital and Sky9 Capital also participating in the &#8220;oversubscribed&#8221; Series A-plus raise. It didn&#8217;t disclose how much it raised from its Series A round. The fresh proceeds will be used for product R&amp;D and user growth in the international market, BUD said.<\/p><div id=\"tc-target-mid-article-2271535\" class=\"tc-target-mid-article ad-unit--size-auto\"><\/div>\n<p>Former Snap engineers <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/shawnxiaolin\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Shawn Lin<\/a> and <a href=\"https:\/\/www.linkedin.com\/in\/risafeng\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Risa Feng<\/a> co-founded BUD in 2019 and have grown the firm into a team of 100 people strong. Their goal is to reach 200 employees by the end of this year and set up a global headquarters in Singapore, which is <a href=\"https:\/\/www.bloomberg.com\/news\/articles\/2021-11-01\/singapore-has-grand-ambitions-to-become-a-global-crypto-hub\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">emerging as a crypto hub<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p>One of BUD&#8217;s selling points is enabling people with no technical background to easily create customized 3D worlds in a drag-and-drop fashion. This isn&#8217;t unlike <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/27\/south-koreas-naver-z-launches-100m-fund-for-metaverse-creators\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Zepeto<\/a>, a popular creator-focused metaverse app under South Korean internet conglomerate Naver. Next door in China, a new 3D-avatar social platform called Zheli (&#8220;Jelly&#8221;) recently topped the free social app category in the Chinese App Store.<\/p>\n<p>While apps like BUD, Roblox and Zepeto are crafting metaverse experiences for end-users, there is a raft of entrepreneurs building the underlying infrastructure that will make the metaverse more viable, rather than <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/03\/over-500-mobile-apps-are-now-using-the-term-metaverse-to-attract-new-users\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">merely a buzzword<\/a>. Some are making decentralized payments systems and others are developing creator tools. In the latter category is Tachi Graphics, which runs a collaboration platform for 3D graphics developers and recently closed a chunky <a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/02\/07\/3d-graphics-infrastructure-taichi-series-a\/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$50 million Series A funding round<\/a>.<\/p>\n<p><em>Updated with more performance data from BUD.<\/em><\/p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"><\/div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"PC84bVl3ng\"><p><a href=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/27\/south-koreas-naver-z-launches-100m-fund-for-metaverse-creators\/\">South Korea&#8217;s Naver Z launches $100M fund for metaverse creators<\/a><\/p><\/blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" style=\"position: absolute; clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);\" title=\"&#8220;South Korea&#8217;s Naver Z launches $100M fund for metaverse creators&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https:\/\/techcrunch.com\/2022\/01\/27\/south-koreas-naver-z-launches-100m-fund-for-metaverse-creators\/embed\/#?secret=vGJhBN2E0p#?secret=PC84bVl3ng\" data-secret=\"PC84bVl3ng\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"><\/iframe><\/div>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n<p><audio style=\"display: none;\" controls=\"controls\"><\/audio><\/p>\n","protected":false},"excerpt":{"rendered":"<p>Investors are justling to find the next killer app for the metaverse.
